The Challenge to Scripture Holders: Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi presents two Quranic challenges as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Quranic challenges to Jews and Christians as independent proofs of the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Scripture holders' refusal of easy challenges proves they knew the Prophet was true.

Maturidi continues his cumulative argument for prophethood by turning to two Quranic challenges. The first challenges the Jews to wish for death, the second challenges the Christians to imprecation (mubahala). Both rely on the opponents' reluctance to engage, which itself testifies to their knowledge of the Prophet's authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the two challenges and the concluding statement. Then read the English translation to ensure understanding.
The passage is concise; each word matters.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find the death-wish challenge (with its two aspects) and the mubahala challenge. Notice how Maturidi presents each as a distinct proof.
The first argument has two aspects: promise of death and refusal to wish.
3
Reflect on why reluctance is proof
Ask yourself: Why does the opponents' failure to accept an easy challenge constitute proof of prophethood? The commentary will clarify the logical force.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج في إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم - مع ما بينا - بقوله لليهود: فتمنوا الموت [البقرة 94] الآية بوجهين أحدهما الوعد بأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا. والثاني أنهم لا يتمنون أبدا، ولا شيء أيسر عليهم من تمنى ذلك؛ وبمباهلة النصارى والإخبار بوقوع اللعن؛ ثبت أنه معلوم النعت في كتبهم.
And he argued for the establishment of the message of Muhammad (peace be upon him) — along with what we have explained — by His saying to the Jews: 'So wish for death' [al-Baqara 94], the verse, in two aspects: one, the promise that if they wished for death they would die; and two, that they would never wish for it, and nothing is easier for them than to wish that; and by the mubahala with the Christians and the foretelling of the occurrence of the curse; it is established that his description is known in their books.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents a further proof from the Quran's challenge to the Jews to wish for death (Surah al-Baqara 94) and the mubahala (imprecation) with the Christians (Surah Al 'Imran 61). Maturidi explains two aspects of the death-wish challenge: first, if they had genuinely wished for death, they would have died; second, the fact that they never wished for death despite its ease shows they knew Muhammad was a true prophet. Similarly, the mubahala event and the foretelling that the curse would fall on the liars came true, proving that the Prophet's description was in their scriptures.

Key Terms
فتمنوا الموت
المباهلة
اللعن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic challenges are just rhetorical, not evidential.
Correction: Maturidi shows they are direct proofs because the opponents' refusal to engage demonstrates their hidden knowledge.

Checkpoint
What are the two aspects of the argument from the verse 'So wish for death'?
A) The Jews would die if they wished, and they never wished
B) The Jews would go to paradise, and they refused
C) The Jews were afraid of death, and they confessed
D) The Jews would be punished, and they accepted

Key Takeaway
The Quranic challenges to scripture holders are leveraged by Maturidi as independent proofs of prophethood, grounded in the opponents' behavior.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews refused to wish for death despite it being easy. Are there simple acts of faith you avoid because you fear the outcome would expose your lack of certainty? What would it take to face that test today?
?
The Christians were challenged to a mubahala. Would you be willing to let God be the judge between you and someone who denies the truth of your beliefs? Why does that thought make you uncomfortable?
?
Maturidi uses the opponents' behavior as evidence of their knowledge. If your actions were examined today, would they testify that you truly believe the Prophet is from God, or would your avoidance of certain tests betray hidden doubts?

Prophethood

The Quran's Inimitability in an Age of Ignorance
Maturidi states the Quran's miraculous nature given the historical context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran's unmatched excellence in a time of widespread idolatry proves it is from Allah.

Core Idea
No human can match the Quran, not even all monotheists combined.

Maturidi starts by reminding us that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was sent when the world was engulfed in idolatry. Yet the Quran emerged with such profound truth and eloquence that all monotheists, past and future, could not produce a tenth of its evidence. This lesson unpacks that powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and notice the historical setting
Identify the era described: tawhid was absent, people worshipped idols. This sets the stage for the miracle.
2
Understand the hyperbole
The author says all monotheists cannot reach a tenth. This is a claim of inimitability (i'jaz).
The phrase 'would not have reached a tenth' is a rhetorical exaggeration emphasizing impossibility.
3
Ask why this proves prophethood
Reflect: if the Quran is beyond human capacity, especially in that environment, then it must be from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا أن رسول الله الله بعث في عصر لم يُعرف فيه التوحيد، بل / كان عباد الأوثان والأصنام والنيران فجميع ما أنزل عليه من القرآن هو من أنجح ما لو اجتمع موحدو العالم من مضى منهم ومَن يكون أبدا، على إظهار أدلته ما احتملت بلوغ عُشرها، فضلاً عن الإحاطة في ذلك الزمان الذي لا يُقدر على موحد واحد . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إن القرآن أنزل في عشرين سنة فصاعدا بالتفاريق؛ ما خرج كله على وزن واحد من النظم، على موافقة بعضه بعضاً مما لو احتمل كون مثله عن الخلق لم يمتنع من الخلق من الاختلاف في شيء من ذلك، دل أنه نزل من عند علام الغيوب. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The basis of this is that the Messenger of Allah was sent in an age in which tawḥīd (monotheism) was not known, rather they were worshippers of idols, statues, and fires. So all that was revealed to him of the Qur'an is among the most triumphant; if all the monotheists of the world, past and future, gathered to produce its evidences, they would not have reached a tenth, let alone encompass it in that time in which not a single monotheist could be found. There is no power except with Allah. Also, the Qur'an was revealed over twenty years or more in parts; it did not come forth entirely upon a single weight of composition, yet its parts agree with one another. If it were possible for the like of it to come from creation, they would not have refrained from disagreement in anything of that. That indicates it was sent down from the Knower of the Unseen. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from the miraculous nature of the Qur'an. Maturidi begins by stating that the Messenger was sent in an age of widespread idolatry, where tawḥīd was virtually absent. Yet the Qur'an is of such high caliber that even all monotheists of all times cannot produce a tenth of its evidence, let alone match it. Then he presents a specific argument: the Qur'an was revealed over twenty years in separate portions, yet it maintains a single harmonious style and its parts agree. If it were possible for humans to produce something like it, they would have disagreed among themselves (as is natural for human composition). This consistency and uniqueness prove it is from Allah, the Knower of the Unseen. The argument relies on the impossibility of human collaboration over such a long period to produce a work with perfect internal harmony and unmatched eloquence.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الإعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Quran's excellence is relative and could be matched by later scholars.
Correction: Maturidi asserts that even all monotheists combined cannot produce a tenth, implying absolute inimitability.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the significance of the Prophet being sent in an age of widespread idolatry?
A) It shows that the Prophet was lucky to find a receptive audience
B) It emphasizes that the Quran's excellence cannot be explained by human sources
C) It indicates that monotheists were the ones who rejected him
D) It proves that the Quran was written by multiple authors

Key Takeaway
The Quran's unmatched excellence in a dark age of idolatry proves it cannot be of human origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If in that age not even a single monotheist could be found, yet the Quran's evidence remains unmatched, what does that say about your own reliance on human intellect apart from divine guidance? Are you seeking the Quran as your ultimate proof, or are you content with human opinions?
?
The passage says all monotheists combined cannot produce a tenth of the Quran's evidences. Do you approach the Quran with such awe and humility, or do you treat it as a book you can easily master? What change in your daily study will reflect this truth?
?
When you read the Quran, are you actively looking for its 'evidences' (adillatihi) that prove its divine origin, or do you read it only for comfort and ritual? How will you train your heart to see the Quran as the ultimate argument that demands your full submission?

The Miracle of the Quran's Internal Consistency
Maturidi argues the Quran's internal harmony over a long period proves divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's consistent style and content, despite being revealed piecemeal over many years, proves it is from Allah.

Core Idea
Human groups inevitably disagree; the Quran's perfect harmony over 20 years is impossible for humans.

Maturidi presents another powerful argument: the Quran was revealed in parts over more than twenty years, yet its composition and meaning are perfectly consistent. Humans working over such a long period would naturally disagree, but the Quran shows no such thing. This lesson explores why this internal harmony is a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the revelation process: over 20 years, in parts, and yet the whole is consistent.
The phrase 'did not come forth upon a single weight of composition' implies the revelations came in different contexts.
2
Identify the argument
The author says if humans produced a similar work, they would have disagreed. The Quran's agreement indicates divine origin.
Consider how human collaborative works often show inconsistencies.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that this points to the Knower of the Unseen (Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا أن رسول الله الله بعث في عصر لم يُعرف فيه التوحيد، بل / كان عباد الأوثان والأصنام والنيران فجميع ما أنزل عليه من القرآن هو من أنجح ما لو اجتمع موحدو العالم من مضى منهم ومَن يكون أبدا، على إظهار أدلته ما احتملت بلوغ عُشرها، فضلاً عن الإحاطة في ذلك الزمان الذي لا يُقدر على موحد واحد . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إن القرآن أنزل في عشرين سنة فصاعدا بالتفاريق؛ ما خرج كله على وزن واحد من النظم، على موافقة بعضه بعضاً مما لو احتمل كون مثله عن الخلق لم يمتنع من الخلق من الاختلاف في شيء من ذلك، دل أنه نزل من عند علام الغيوب. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The basis of this is that the Messenger of Allah was sent in an age in which tawḥīd (monotheism) was not known, rather they were worshippers of idols, statues, and fires. So all that was revealed to him of the Qur'an is among the most triumphant; if all the monotheists of the world, past and future, gathered to produce its evidences, they would not have reached a tenth, let alone encompass it in that time in which not a single monotheist could be found. There is no power except with Allah. Also, the Qur'an was revealed over twenty years or more in parts; it did not come forth entirely upon a single weight of composition, yet its parts agree with one another. If it were possible for the like of it to come from creation, they would not have refrained from disagreement in anything of that. That indicates it was sent down from the Knower of the Unseen. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from the miraculous nature of the Qur'an. Maturidi begins by stating that the Messenger was sent in an age of widespread idolatry, where tawḥīd was virtually absent. Yet the Qur'an is of such high caliber that even all monotheists of all times cannot produce a tenth of its evidence, let alone match it. Then he presents a specific argument: the Qur'an was revealed over twenty years in separate portions, yet it maintains a single harmonious style and its parts agree. If it were possible for humans to produce something like it, they would have disagreed among themselves (as is natural for human composition). This consistency and uniqueness prove it is from Allah, the Knower of the Unseen. The argument relies on the impossibility of human collaboration over such a long period to produce a work with perfect internal harmony and unmatched eloquence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might argue that editorial revision could reconcile inconsistencies in a human work.
Correction: Maturidi points out that over 20 years, human authors would naturally change their minds or make errors; the Quran's perfection defies that.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what indicates that the Quran is from Allah?
A) It was revealed over 20 years
B) Its parts agree with each other despite being revealed over time
C) It was revealed to an illiterate prophet
D) It contains laws

Key Takeaway
The Quran's flawless internal consistency, despite piecemeal revelation over decades, is a sign of divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe the Quran is from the Knower of the Unseen because of its perfect consistency, why do you still let your own opinions and desires contradict its commands in your daily life?
?
When you encounter a seeming inconsistency in the Quran, do you immediately assume your own understanding is flawed, or do you entertain doubts? What would it take for you to fully trust its consistency as a sign from Allah?
?
The Quran was revealed over 20 years yet is perfectly harmonious. Your own life over the past 20 years is likely full of contradictions and changes. What does this contrast reveal about your need for divine guidance rather than relying on your own consistency?

The Two Proofs: The Verse and the Mubahala
Maturidi enumerates two proofs for Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two proofs from the Quran and the mubahala that Maturidi uses to establish the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The Jews' refusal to wish for death and the Christian mubahala are clear signs confirming the Prophet's truth.

Maturidi presents two powerful arguments for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from the Quran and from the practice of mubahala with the Christians. These proofs are drawn from the Jews' own claim and the Christians' own scriptures. Let's examine how these arguments work.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Maturidi presents two distinct proofs: one from the verse addressed to the Jews, and one from the mubahala with the Christians.
The passage begins with 'واحتج في إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم'.
2
Identify the first proof
Identify the verse 'fatanaw al-mawt' and the two aspects Maturidi extracts: the promise of death if they wished, and the fact they will never wish despite ease.
This proof challenges the Jews directly from their own scripture.
3
Identify the second proof
Find the mubahala proof: the Prophet invoked a curse (mubahala) with the Christians, and it was known from their scriptures that he would be vindicated.
The mubahala serves as a practical demonstration of truth.
4
Reflect on the logic
Consider why each proof is compelling. The first proof is a direct challenge that the Jews cannot fulfill. The second proof involves a reciprocal curse that would have harmed the Christians if they were false.
These proofs are based on observable behavior and scriptural knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج في إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم - مع ما بينا - بقوله لليهود: فتمنوا الموت [البقرة، ٩٤/٢] الآية بوجهين أحدهما الوعد بأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا. والثاني أنهم لا يتمنون أبدا، ولا شيء أيسر عليهم من تمنى ذلك ؛ وبمباهلة النصارى والإخبار بوقوع اللعن "؛ ثبت أنه معلوم النعت في كتبهم. فأدخل الوراق [عليه] أنهم لو تمنوا باللسان لقيل : إنما أريد به القلب. والثاني أنهم قد آمنوا بموسى وعيسى، وقد أخبراهم بذلك " كما يخبر المنجمة " فجواب الأول أن المباهلة لا تحتمل ذلك ، وأيضا إنهم أهل بصر، إذ لو ردّوا لقابلوا بأنهم فعلوا ذلك أيضاً بقلوبهم. والحرف الثاني لو كان كذلك ما امتنعوا عن مقابلته عند قوله: التدخلن المسجد الحرام ﴾ [الفتح، ٢٧/٤٨] ، وقوله : ليظهره على الدين كله ﴾ [الفتح، ٢٨/٤٨]؛ ولو كان بذلك كان التصديق لما احتمل المقابلة بأعز الأشياء، وهي النفس والأموال. {قال الفقيه رحمه الله : } وأيضا إنه لو كان بالذي / ذكر ، لم يكن خبر رسول الله «لن [١٠١ظ] يتمنوه» بذلك ، بل كان بالذي يعلم أنهم لا يفعلون. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
He argued in proving the message of Muhammad peace be upon him—along with what we have stated—by His saying to the Jews: 'So wish for death' [Quran 2:94], the verse in two aspects: one is the promise that if they wished for death they would die. The second is that they will never wish for it, and nothing is easier for them than wishing that. And by the mubāhala (mutual imprecation) with the Christians and the inform that the curse will occur; this confirms that his description was known in their scriptures. Then al-Warrāq objected: if they wished verbally, it would be said that only the heart was intended. Second: they believed in Moses and Jesus, and they informed them of that, just as the astrologer informs. The answer to the first is that the mubāhala does not bear that. Also, they were people of insight, for if they refused they could respond that they did that also with their hearts. As for the second point, if it were so, they would not have refrained from confronting him when He said: 'You will enter the Sacred Mosque' [Quran 48:27] and His saying: 'He will make it prevail over all religion' [Quran 48:28]; and if it were by that, the confirmation would not have borne confronting with the dearest things, namely life and wealth. Al-Faqīh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Also, if it were as mentioned, the report of the Messenger of Allah 'they will never wish for it' would not be by that; rather it would be by that which he knows they will not do. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a combination of proofs and refutations of objections. Maturidi first presents two proofs for Muhammad's prophethood: (1) the verse 'fatanaw al-mawt' (Quran 2:94) addressing the Jews, with two aspects—if they wish for death they would die, and they will never wish for it even though it is easy; (2) the mubāhala with the Christians where the prophet invoked a curse, and it was known in their scriptures. Then al-Warrāq objects: the first proof (the verse) could be interpreted as merely verbal while the heart intended something else; and the second proof (Christian prophecies) is like astrologers' predictions. The answer: the mubāhala cannot be reduced to verbal intent because it involves a curse; the Christians were insightful and would have presented the same claim if they could. For the second objection, if the confirmation were merely like astrologers' predictions, they would not have risked their lives and wealth—as seen from the prophecies about entering the mosque and the religion prevailing. Al-Faqīh adds: the Prophet's statement 'they will never wish for it' was not based on mere knowledge of their inaction but was a divine challenge. Thus the objections are refuted.

Key Terms
فتمنوا الموت
المباهلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the verse 'wish for death' was only a rhetorical challenge without real consequences.
Correction: Maturidi shows it was a literal promise and a test of sincerity, as the Jews' avoidance demonstrates their false claim.

Checkpoint
What are the two aspects of the verse 'fatanaw al-mawt' according to Maturidi?
A) The Jews will wish for death and die, and they will do so repeatedly
B) If they wished for death they would die, and they will never wish for it
C) The verse is abrogated and no longer applies
D) The Jews actually wished for death but did not die

Key Takeaway
The Jews' failure to wish for death and the Christians' avoidance of mubahala are compelling, observable proofs of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had been among the Jews or Christians addressed by these challenges, would you have been willing to test your claim? What does your answer reveal about the certainty of your own faith?
?
Have you ever avoided a situation that would put your beliefs to the test, even though you knew it would confirm truth? What holds you back from seeking such proofs in your own life?

Refuting Al-Warraq's Objections
Maturidi refutes al-Warraq's objections regarding verbal intent and scriptural predictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Warraq's objections to the proofs and Maturidi's responses, demonstrating the robustness of the arguments.

Core Idea
Al-Warraq's objections fail because the mubahala is not merely verbal and prophecies led to real sacrifice.

After presenting proofs, Maturidi addresses objections raised by al-Warraq. These objections try to weaken the force of the miracle by suggesting mere verbal agreement or astrologer-like predictions. Maturidi's refutations show why these criticisms miss the mark.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Read al-Warraq's two objections: first, the Jews' wish could be merely verbal (intended by heart); second, the Christian prophecies are like astrologers' predictions.
Notice how al-Warraq tries to reduce the miracle to ordinary phenomena.
2
Study the first answer
Maturidi answers that the mubahala cannot be merely verbal because it involves a curse—something serious. Also, the Christians were insightful; they could have claimed they did it with their hearts if it were possible.
The mubahala's gravity prevents it from being a mere verbal formality.
3
Study the second answer
Maturidi responds that if the prophecies were like astrologers, the Christians would have risked confronting the Prophet despite predictions. But they did not, showing the prophecies were definitive.
The willingness to risk life and wealth is evidence of certainty.
4
Consider al-Faqih's addition
Al-Faqih adds that the Prophet's statement 'they will never wish for it' was not based on mere knowledge but a divine declaration, further undermining al-Warraq's interpretation.
This reinforces the miraculous nature of the challenge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج في إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم - مع ما بينا - بقوله لليهود: فتمنوا الموت [البقرة، ٩٤/٢] الآية بوجهين أحدهما الوعد بأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا. والثاني أنهم لا يتمنون أبدا، ولا شيء أيسر عليهم من تمنى ذلك ؛ وبمباهلة النصارى والإخبار بوقوع اللعن "؛ ثبت أنه معلوم النعت في كتبهم. فأدخل الوراق [عليه] أنهم لو تمنوا باللسان لقيل : إنما أريد به القلب. والثاني أنهم قد آمنوا بموسى وعيسى، وقد أخبراهم بذلك " كما يخبر المنجمة " فجواب الأول أن المباهلة لا تحتمل ذلك ، وأيضا إنهم أهل بصر، إذ لو ردّوا لقابلوا بأنهم فعلوا ذلك أيضاً بقلوبهم. والحرف الثاني لو كان كذلك ما امتنعوا عن مقابلته عند قوله: التدخلن المسجد الحرام ﴾ [الفتح، ٢٧/٤٨] ، وقوله : ليظهره على الدين كله ﴾ [الفتح، ٢٨/٤٨]؛ ولو كان بذلك كان التصديق لما احتمل المقابلة بأعز الأشياء، وهي النفس والأموال. {قال الفقيه رحمه الله : } وأيضا إنه لو كان بالذي / ذكر ، لم يكن خبر رسول الله «لن [١٠١ظ] يتمنوه» بذلك ، بل كان بالذي يعلم أنهم لا يفعلون. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
He argued in proving the message of Muhammad peace be upon him—along with what we have stated—by His saying to the Jews: 'So wish for death' [Quran 2:94], the verse in two aspects: one is the promise that if they wished for death they would die. The second is that they will never wish for it, and nothing is easier for them than wishing that. And by the mubāhala (mutual imprecation) with the Christians and the inform that the curse will occur; this confirms that his description was known in their scriptures. Then al-Warrāq objected: if they wished verbally, it would be said that only the heart was intended. Second: they believed in Moses and Jesus, and they informed them of that, just as the astrologer informs. The answer to the first is that the mubāhala does not bear that. Also, they were people of insight, for if they refused they could respond that they did that also with their hearts. As for the second point, if it were so, they would not have refrained from confronting him when He said: 'You will enter the Sacred Mosque' [Quran 48:27] and His saying: 'He will make it prevail over all religion' [Quran 48:28]; and if it were by that, the confirmation would not have borne confronting with the dearest things, namely life and wealth. Al-Faqīh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Also, if it were as mentioned, the report of the Messenger of Allah 'they will never wish for it' would not be by that; rather it would be by that which he knows they will not do. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a combination of proofs and refutations of objections. Maturidi first presents two proofs for Muhammad's prophethood: (1) the verse 'fatanaw al-mawt' (Quran 2:94) addressing the Jews, with two aspects—if they wish for death they would die, and they will never wish for it even though it is easy; (2) the mubāhala with the Christians where the prophet invoked a curse, and it was known in their scriptures. Then al-Warrāq objects: the first proof (the verse) could be interpreted as merely verbal while the heart intended something else; and the second proof (Christian prophecies) is like astrologers' predictions. The answer: the mubāhala cannot be reduced to verbal intent because it involves a curse; the Christians were insightful and would have presented the same claim if they could. For the second objection, if the confirmation were merely like astrologers' predictions, they would not have risked their lives and wealth—as seen from the prophecies about entering the mosque and the religion prevailing. Al-Faqīh adds: the Prophet's statement 'they will never wish for it' was not based on mere knowledge of their inaction but was a divine challenge. Thus the objections are refuted.

Key Terms
الوراق
المباهلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that prophecies from previous scriptures are merely predictions like those of astrologers, with no special miracle.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the prophecies led to real-world confrontations where people risked their lives, proving they were taken as certain, not mere possibilities.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi refute al-Warraq's first objection that the Jews' wish could be merely verbal?
A) He says the mubahala is too serious to be merely verbal
B) He argues that the Jews were liars
C) He says the Quranic verse was abrogated
D) He relies on consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Al-Warraq's objections fail because the mubahala is inherently serious and the prophecies led to life-and-death confrontations, confirming their miraculous nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear sophisticated objections to Islam, does your faith ever waver? How does Maturidi's example of taking objections seriously yet refuting them compel you to deepen your own understanding so you are not shaken?
?
The mubahala was a life-and-death challenge. Do you treat the truth of Islam as casually, or are you willing to risk everything for it? What is one thing today you can sacrifice for your faith?
?
The prophecies led people to risk their lives. Do you live as if Allah's promises—like His help or reward—are absolutely certain, or do you sometimes act as if they are distant possibilities? What would change if you truly believed them right now?

Refuting the Astrology Analogy for Prophethood
Maturidi refutes the analogy of prophethood to astrology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that Muhammad's prophethood is analogous to astrology.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not guesswork; the challenge was a real threat.

The objector likened Muhammad's call to astrologers' predictions. Maturidi responds that if it were mere speculation, people would not have hesitated to answer the challenge. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to see Maturidi's argument.
2
Understand the objection
The objector says prophethood is like astrology, i.e., baseless.
3
Follow the refutation
Maturidi argues that if it were like astrology, people wouldn't be hesitant; their hesitation shows it was not baseless.
4
Grasp the significance
This shows the unique nature of prophethood and the challenge's authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن ؛ ولو كان على حكم قول المنجمة لما تقرر عندهم حتى يتحرجوا الإجابة. ولم يكن الذي جاء به رسول الله بدون ذلك، [لم] لم يتحرجوا عما خوّفهم فيسلموا؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله . وطعن في قوله وما كنت تتلو من قبله من كتاب [العنكبوت، ٤٨/٢٩] الآية " : إن الحفظ يقوم مقام الكتاب. وأحال ، لأن الحفظ يكون عن تلاوة، وما بالإلقاء عليه فهو عن كتاب يُقرأ " . وبعد، فإنما ذلك إنما يكون بمن يظهر اختلافه "" عند من يعرف به، ومعلوم أنه " نشأ بين أظهرهم [و] لم يُعرف في شيء من ذلك. ولولا ذلك لكان هذا القدر من المقابلة سهلاً لا يعجزون عنه .
He also objected: if it were according to the judgment of the astrologer, they would not have been established with them until they were too hesitant to answer. And what the Messenger of Allah brought was not without that; did they not hesitate to respond to what he threatened them with, so they would submit? There is no power except with Allah. And he objected to His saying, 'And you did not recite before it any scripture' [Quran 29:48] verse: 'Verily, memorization takes the place of a book.' And he rejected it, because memorization arises from recitation, and what is inspired to him is from a book that is read. Moreover, that only occurs for one whose difference appears to those who know him, and it is known that he grew up among them and was not known for any of that. Otherwise, this amount of competition would be easy and they would not be incapable of it.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents two further objections from al-Warrāq (or Ibn al-Rawandi) and their refutations. First objection: the prophethood of Muhammad is like astrology; if it were, people would not be hesitant to respond to the challenge. Maturidi replies that the Prophet's message and threats were not without basis; if it were mere astrology, they would not have hesitated to respond and would have submitted. Second objection: the Quranic verse 'You did not recite any scripture before it' (29:48) is about Muhammad being unlettered, but the objector claims that memorization could substitute for reading from a book. Maturidi refutes this because memorization is based on recitation, and what was revealed to him came from a read book (i.e., the Preserved Tablet). Furthermore, if he had learned from others, his teacher would be known, but he lived among them and was not known for any such learning. If they could have produced similar speech, they would have, but they were incapable. Thus the objections are invalid.

Key Terms
المنجمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue about the astrology analogy?
A) He accepts it as valid
B) He argues that people's hesitation disproves it
C) He says astrology is true
D) He ignores the objection

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the astrology analogy by showing that people's hesitation to respond to the challenge indicates the unique nature of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the message of the Qur'an, do you find yourself hesitating to act? Is your hesitation due to uncertainty about its truth, or because you know it is true and demands change? What will you do today to move from hesitation to submission?
?
The Quraysh hesitated because they realized the Prophet's warning was unlike an astrologer's guess—it carried real threat. Do you treat the warnings of the Hereafter as real and urgent, or do you dismiss them as mere speculation? How will you change your daily life to reflect that urgency?
?
If you were to honestly examine your heart, would you find that you sometimes treat the Prophet's commands like astrological predictions—optional and without consequence? What is one command you have been ignoring or delaying? Will you act on it today, acknowledging that it comes from the One who truly threatens and promises?

Refuting the Claim that Memorization Equals Revelation
Maturidi refutes the claim that memorization could substitute for revelation from a book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that memorization could substitute for the Quran being revealed from a book.

Core Idea
Memorization presupposes recitation; the Prophet received revelation directly.

The objector argued that the Quranic verse 'You did not recite any scripture before it' could be negated by the Prophet memorizing from others. Maturidi refutes this by showing that memorization arises from recitation, and the Prophet's learning was not from a known teacher. This lesson examines the logic behind the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
2
Identify the objection
The objector claims memorization can replace reading from a book.
3
Follow the first refutation
Maturidi says memorization comes from recitation, so it cannot come from nothing.
4
Follow the second refutation
If the Prophet had a teacher, he would be known; but he was not known for learning from anyone.
5

The inability of opponents to produce similar speech shows its divine origin.

The First Answer: Mubahala and Insight
Maturidi's first answer about mubahala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first argument that the mubahala challenge itself disproves the objection because the opponents were insightful and could have claimed inward belief.

Core Idea
The mubahala challenge exposes the opponents' lack of true faith.

This lesson examines Maturidi's first response to an objection concerning the mubahala incident. He argues that the very nature of the mubahala precludes the objection, as the opponents were insightful people who could have easily countered if they had any ground.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source text and its translation to grasp the first answer.
Notice the concise style of Maturidi.
2
Understand the implied objection
Consider what objection Maturidi is answering: perhaps that outward acceptance could be feigned.
3
Analyze the logic of the mubahala
Maturidi says the mubahala does not admit that objection because the opponents were insightful (ahl basar). If they had rejected, they could have claimed they believed inwardly.
The mubahala is a mutual imprecation; those who are wrong would be cursed.
4
Reflect on the strength of the argument
Consider how this argument turns the objection back on the opponents: their failure to use that counter shows their disbelief was genuine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فجواب الأول أن المباهلة لا تحتمل ذلك، وأيضا إنهم أهل بصر، إذ لو ردوا لقابلوا بأنهم فعلوا ذلك أيضا بقلوبهم. والحرف الثاني لو كان كذلك ما امتنعوا عن مقابلته عند قوله: {لتدخلن المسجد الحرام} [الفتح: ٢٧]، وقوله: {ليظهره على الدين كله} [الفتح: ٢٨]؛ ولو كان بذلك كان التصديق لما احتمل المقابلة بأعز الأشياء، وهي النفس والأموال.
The first answer is that the mubahala does not admit that. Also, they were people of insight, for if they had rejected, they would have countered by saying that they also did that with their hearts. The second point: if it were so, they would not have refrained from opposing it when He said: 'You will certainly enter the Sacred Mosque' [al-Fath 27] and His saying: 'That He may make it prevail over all religion' [al-Fath 28]; and if it were that, the belief would not have admitted the opposition with the most precious things, namely life and wealth.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents two answers to an objection concerning the mubahala (imprecation) and a prophetic prediction. The first answer argues that the mubahala itself precludes the objection because the opponents were insightful; had they rejected the challenge, they could have simply claimed they also believed inwardly. The second answer points to Quranic verses promising entry into Mecca and the triumph of Islam—if the opponents' belief had been merely outward, they would not have risked their lives and wealth in opposition. The argument is that their willingness to sacrifice proves the sincerity of their disbelief, contradicting the objection.

Key Terms
المباهلة
أهل بصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's first answer uses the mubahala challenge and the opponents' insight to prove that their disbelief was genuine, not feigned.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Maturidi's second answer using victory verses.

The Faqih's Argument: Prophetic Knowledge as Proof
Al-Faqih argues that the Prophet's knowledge of the Jews' unwillingness to wish for death proves the truth of his message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Faqih uses the Prophet's knowledge of the Jews' reluctance to wish for death as evidence for the truth of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's certain knowledge proves his message is from Allah.

Al-Faqih responds to an objection by pointing out that the Prophet's statement about the Jews not wishing for death cannot be based on conjecture; it is a certainty known only through revelation. This short but powerful argument demonstrates the logical foundation for accepting prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of al-Faqih.
2
Identify the objection being refuted
The passage begins with 'if it were as mentioned' — this refers to an objection that the Prophet's knowledge is like that of an astrologer. Try to infer what that objection might be.
3
Analyze the logical structure
Al-Faqih presents a conditional argument: if the Prophet's knowledge were conjectural, then his report would not be certain. But the report is certain, so the premise is false. Trace this logic.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the implication for prophethood
Consider what this argument implies about the source of the Prophet's knowledge. How does it establish the truth of his prophethood?
The closing phrase 'there is no power except with Allah' affirms reliance on Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
{قال الفقيه رحمه الله:} وأيضا إنه لو كان بالذي ذكر، لم يكن خبر رسول الله «لن يتمنوه» بذلك، بل كان بالذي يعلم أنهم لا يفعلون. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
{Al-Faqih, may Allah have mercy on him, said:} And also, if it were as mentioned, then the report of the Messenger of Allah, 'they will never wish for it,' would not be like that, but rather it would be based on what He knows that they will not do. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This is a brief argument from al-Faqih. He responds to an objection about the authenticity of prophetic reports. The argument is that if the Prophet's knowledge were like that of an astrologer (as claimed by the objector), then his statement 'they will never wish for it' (referring to the Jews' wish for death) would not be certain. But the Prophet knew with certainty that they would not wish for death, which proves his knowledge is from Allah, not from conjecture. The phrase 'there is no power except with Allah' is a closing invocation.

Key Terms
الفقيه
خبر رسول الله
لن يتمنوه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is a general statement about hadith authenticity.
Correction: This is not a general statement about hadith authenticity but a specific rebuttal to an objection about the nature of prophetic knowledge.

Checkpoint
What does al-Faqih argue about the Prophet's knowledge of the Jews not wishing for death?
A) It was based on astrological prediction.
B) It was based on divine knowledge, not guesswork.
C) It was a lucky guess.
D) It was learned from the Jews themselves.

Key Takeaway
Al-Faqih's argument shows that the Prophet's knowledge of unseen matters, such as the Jews' inner state, is a sign of divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Faqih's argument shows that even a single statement of the Prophet is enough to disprove a false premise. Are there areas of your faith where you allow doubts to linger despite clear prophetic texts? What step will you take to remove that doubt?

The Prophet’s Predictions Are Not Astrological Guesses
Maturidi refutes the objection that the Prophet’s predictions resemble astrological guesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hesitation of the Prophet’s opponents proves that his message is divine, not astrological.

Core Idea
Opponents’ fear shows the Prophet’s message is from Allah, not from guesswork.

Imam Maturidi responds to an objection that the Prophet’s predictions resemble those of astrologers. He points to the strong effect they had on the listeners, which astrologers’ claims never achieve. This lesson unpacks this logical rebuttal from Kitàb al-Tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and rebuttal
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the conditional argument and the rhetorical question.
The word [لم] is uncertain but the logic is clear.
2
Understand the logical structure
Identify the condition (if astrological, no hesitation) and the actual outcome (hesitation occurred). The conclusion is that it cannot be astrological.
3
Reflect on the closing phrase
Consider why Maturidi ends with "Wa la hawla wala quwwata illa billah." This affirms divine power behind the Prophet’s message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن؛ ولو كان على حكم قول المنجمة لما تقرر عندهم حتى يتحرجوا الإجابة. ولم يكن الذي جاء به رسول الله بدون ذلك، [لم] لم يتحرجوا عما خوفهم فيسلموا؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And he objected: And if it were according to the saying of the astrologer, it would not be established with them such that they would hesitate to answer. And what the Messenger of Allah brought was not without that; [did] they not hesitate due to what he frightened them with and then submit? And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage contains an objection (possibly from the Warraq) and a rebuttal. The objection suggests that the Prophet's predictions could be like those of an astrologer. The rebuttal uses a logical dilemma: if the Prophet's predictions were merely astrological, they would not have been so deeply established in the hearts of the opponents that they would hesitate to respond or become frightened. The fact that the opponents did hesitate and did not submit despite the Prophet's warnings indicates that his message was not of human origin. The closing phrase 'there is no power except with Allah' emphasizes divine assistance.

Key Terms

الطعن
التحرج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet’s predictions could be based on astrological calculations.
Correction: The Prophet’s predictions caused such deep hesitation and fear that astrological claims could never produce; this proves they were divinely revealed.

What does Maturidi use to disprove the astrologer objection?
A) The Prophet’s miracles
B) The opponents’ hesitation to respond
C) The weakness of astrology
D) The number of predictions

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's predictions had a real impact that astrologers' claims cannot achieve, proving their divine origin.

Refuting the Memorization Objection to the Prophet's Revelation
Maturidi refutes the objection that memorization can substitute for recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the objection that the Prophet could have memorized previous scriptures instead of receiving direct revelation.

Core Idea
Memorization presupposes recitation; the Prophet's knowledge came from Allah, not from any book.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle objection to the Quranic claim that the Prophet did not recite any book before the Quran. The objector tries to sidestep the verse by suggesting that memorization could replace recitation. Maturidi shows why this fails, using both logical and historical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
Start by reading the verse (al-Ankabut 29:48) and the objection raised against it. The objector claims that memorization could substitute for recitation.
The verse is clear: the Prophet did not recite any prior scripture.
2
Analyze Maturidi's first refutation
Maturidi argues that memorization depends on recitation—one cannot memorize a book without having recited it first. Therefore, the Prophet's knowledge could not come from memorization of previous scriptures.
This is a logical refutation based on the nature of memorization.
3
Examine the second refutation
Maturidi adds that the Prophet grew up among the Arabs and was never known for studying with scholars of previous scriptures. If he had learned from them, it would have been evident.
This historical evidence reinforces the logical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن في قوله: {وما كنت تتلو من قبله من كتاب} [العنكبوت: ٤٨] الآية: «إن الحفظ يقوم مقام الكتاب». وأحال، لأن الحفظ يكون عن تلاوة، وما بالإلقاء عليه فهو عن كتاب يقرأ. وبعد، فإنما ذلك إنما يكون بمن يظهر اختلافه عند من يعرف به، ومعلوم أنه نشأ بين أظهرهم [و] لم يعرف في شيء من ذلك. ولولا ذلك لكان هذا القدر من المقابلة سهلا لا يعجزون عنه.
And he objected regarding His saying: 'And you did not recite before it any book' [al-Ankabut 48] the verse: 'Indeed, memorization takes the place of the Book.' And he declared it impossible, because memorization comes from recitation, and what is inspired to him is from a Book that is read. Moreover, that only occurs with one who shows his difference to those who know him, and it is known that he grew up among them and was not known for any of that. And were it not for that, this amount of opposition would have been easy and they would not have been incapable of it.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage deals with an objection to the Quranic verse that states the Prophet did not recite any book before the Quran. The objector argues that memorization could substitute for recitation, implying the Prophet could have memorized from earlier scriptures. Maturidi refutes this by stating that memorization depends on recitation; the Prophet received revelation directly, not from reading a book. Furthermore, the objector's claim would require the Prophet to have been known for studying with scholars, but he grew up among the Arabs with no such reputation. If the objection were valid, the opponents would have easily produced a similar challenge, but they could not.

Key Terms
الحفظ
التلاوة
الإلقاء
المقابلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet could have memorized previous scriptures without reciting them, thus the verse is not conclusive.
Correction: Memorization depends on recitation; the Prophet received revelation directly, not from any book. Also, his life showed no such study.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi refute the objection about memorization replacing recitation?
A) He agrees that memorization suffices.
B) He argues that memorization requires prior recitation, and the Prophet did not have that.
C) He says the Prophet was illiterate.
D) He claims the Prophet had no memory.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that memorization cannot replace recitation, and the Prophet's known life disproves any claim of prior scripture study.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the Prophet never learned from any human source, how would you expect your relationship with the Quran to differ from how you treat any other book? What concrete change will you make today to honor that belief?
?
The Prophet's life was an open book; his integrity and lack of prior knowledge were undeniable to his contemporaries. Do you live your life with such transparency that people can see your reliance on Allah rather than on your own efforts? What area of your life do you need to bring into the light?
?
Maturidi argues that even memorization implies prior recitation. In your spiritual life, do you rely on 'memorized' actions—rituals without presence—rather than a direct, living connection with the Revealer? What would it mean for you to receive guidance as if directly from Allah today?

Prophethood

The Inevitable Spread of Prophetic Reports
Maturidi argues that prophetic reports spread necessarily and cannot be isolated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the reports of the prophets cannot be considered isolated (āḥād) but are necessarily widespread due to their extraordinary nature.

Core Idea
Extraordinary prophetic reports compel widespread dissemination, refuting the claim of isolated transmission.

Maturidi begins by establishing a general principle: when an extraordinary event occurs, its report spreads irresistibly. He applies this to the prophets, whose miracles and messages are so striking that they cannot be concealed. This lesson examines how the truth of prophetic reports is distinguished from falsehood, using the example of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) to demonstrate that his mission reached every corner, making the charge of isolated reports untenable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of Maturidi's argument.
2
Identify the key claim
Notice that Maturidi argues that reports of prophets spread widely because they are outside the customary. Find the sentence that states this.
The phrase 'ذلك الخارجة عن الأمر المعتاد' is key.
3
Understand the proof from the Prophet
Maturidi uses the example of the Prophet Muhammad: his influence reached all areas, so his reports cannot be isolated. Reflect on why this refutes the objection.
The proof is based on historical observation.
4
Distinguish the type of report
Contrast the ordinary reports with the extraordinary. A single report about an important matter spreads more. Understand this hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك الخارجة عن الأمر المعتاد عندهم ، فيظهر أخبارهم فتنتشر حتى تبلغ أقاصي الدنيا وأدانيها؛ إذ هي على وجه لا يملك السامعون كتمانها، على ما ذكرت من تقاضى الخلقة في نشر مثله . ما قد مع ينتشر مثل ما ذكرت مما لا منفعة فيه، فالذى يعمّ الخلق جميعا معناه أحق في ذلك. وفي كل أمر منتشر عن أحد يعود الخبر إن كان على حق أو جور، فيُعلم ما افتعل منه فيغيّر، وما صدق فيه فيُقَر. وفي ذلك لزوم انتشار أخبار الرسل في حياتهم وظهور المفتعل من فيمحى أثره بالنهي والتغيير ، ويبقى الحق الصدق منه. دليل ذلك أمر رسول الله لا تأتى ناحية نائية ولا مكانًا بعيداً إلا وجدت أثره فيه ظاهرا ، وبخاصة في عصره، إذ كان ينتاب إليه من الآفاق ويظهر شأنه في البلاد؛ فإذا كان كذلك لا وجه لقوله : «أخباره أخبار الآحاد ، ولا لما ذكر من الوجوه، بل الخبر الواحد في الأمر المهم أو الخارج عن الأمر المعتاد ينتشر انتشارا أظهر ، فكيف فيما فيه دعاء أهل الأديان، وإرسال الكتب إلى الأفق، ومجيء الوفود من كل النواحي، وامتحان الرسل بأنواع الحجاج، وقصد الملوك نحوهم في إطفاء نورهم إشفاقاً منهم على ملكهم أن يذهب ويضمحل؛ على ما عرفوا من ضعفهم في أبدانهم وقلة أعوانهم من جوهرهم، فما ذلك الخوف إلا لعلمهم أنهم أتوا من عند القادر العليم. وعلى ذلك ما يخرج مخرج الآيات من الأمور الخطرة لن يذهب أثر ذلك ما بقى لهم تبع ، وبمثله احتجاج . ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما ذكر من إجماعات اليهود والنصارى إنما ذلك في أمور اختلفوا فيها على قدر ما احتمل آراؤهم فانتشرت في أتباع كل منهم، ليس ذلك في الآيات ولا في الأمور الخطرة. وبعد، فإنه متى بلغ ذلك تبديل الشرع حتى كاد أن يمحو أثره ويندرس خبره يفضل الله بمنّه في إرسال من يُحيى ذلك ويُظهر ما عليه الرسل بالآيات القاهرة العقول، ليعلموا بهم التغيير والتبديل، وعلى ذلك الانتشار. ثم من حكم الله أن يختم بمحمد عليه السلام النبوة، وأن لا يرسل إلى أمته بعده رسولاً، جعل أمته بحيث لا يحتمل تغيّر الأمور الجسيمة، ومن عليهم بكتاب حَفِظَهُ ، يُعلَم به التغيير والتبديل، فتبقى شريعته إلى فناء العالم. وبالله التوفيق.
That which is outside the customary matter with them, so their reports appear and spread until they reach the farthest and nearest parts of the world; because they are in a manner that the hearers cannot conceal them, as I mentioned of the demand of creation in spreading the like. Something spreads as I mentioned without benefit, so that which encompasses all people in meaning is more entitled to that. And in every matter spread from someone, the report is examined whether it is truth or falsehood, so what is fabricated from it is known and changed, and what is true in it is confirmed. So from that originates the necessity of the spreading of the reports of the prophets during their lives and the appearance of what is fabricated so its trace is erased by prohibition and change, and the true truth remains. The proof of that is the matter of the Messenger of God: no remote area or distant place comes but you find his trace apparent in it, especially in his era, for people would come to him from horizons and his affair would appear in the lands. Since that is the case, there is no basis for his saying: 'His reports are isolated reports,' nor for what he mentioned of aspects; rather the single report concerning an important matter or what is outside the customary spreads more manifestly, so how about that which involves the call of the people of religions, sending books to horizons, the coming of delegations from every direction, the testing of prophets with various arguments, the kings aiming at extinguishing their light out of fear for their kingdom that it might go and vanish—according to what they knew of their weakness in bodies and their paucity of helpers from their essence—so that fear is only because they knew that they came from the Powerful, the Knowing. And similarly, what comes forth as miracles from perilous matters: its trace will not go as long as they have followers, and by such is argumentation. And there is no power but in God. And what was mentioned of the consensuses of Jews and Christians, that is only in matters in which they differed according to what their opinions allowed, and it spread among the followers of each of them, not in the signs nor in the perilous matters. Then, whenever that reaches the point of altering the divine law so that its trace almost erases and its report becomes obliterated, God favors by His grace in sending one who revives that and shows what the prophets were upon with signs that overwhelm intellects, so that they may know by them the change and alteration, and upon that is the spreading. Then it is of God's decree that He sealed prophethood with Muhammad, peace be upon him, and that he would not send a messenger to his nation after him, so He made his nation such that it cannot undergo alteration of grave matters, and He bestowed upon them a book which He preserved, by which alteration and change is known, so his law remains until the annihilation of the world. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the reports of the prophets are not isolated (āḥād) but are widely transmitted (mutawātir). Maturidi begins by stating that the miraculous affairs of the prophets appear and spread irresistibly, reaching all corners of the world because their nature compels hearers to spread them. He then argues that when any report spreads—whether true or false—people can distinguish fabrication from truth, and the truth remains. This is particularly true for prophets: their reports spread during their lifetimes, and any falsehood is quickly exposed and removed, while the truth persists. The proof is the Prophet Muhammad (pbuh): his influence reached everywhere, so it is impossible to claim his reports are isolated. Moreover, the very nature of prophethood—calling people of all religions, sending letters, receiving delegations, and the fear of kings—proves that such momentous events cannot be hidden. The kings feared the prophets despite their apparent weakness, knowing they came from God. Then Maturidi contrasts the consensus of Jews and Christians: their disagreements spread only in their own followers, not in the divine signs. Finally, he explains that God preserves the religion by sending renewers when needed, and sealed prophethood with Muhammad, giving the Quran as a preserved guide until the end of time.

Key Terms
المعتاد (customary)
المفتعل (fabricated)
خبر الآحاد (isolated report)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The reports of prophets are only considered reliable if they are transmitted by a large number of people at each generation.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the extraordinary nature of the prophetic event itself compels widespread dissemination, making the requirement of numerical multiplicity unnecessary.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the reason why the reports of the prophets cannot be considered isolated (āḥād)?
A) Because the prophets commanded their followers to spread them
B) Because they involve extraordinary matters that compel widespread dissemination
C) Because the Quran explicitly states they are mutawātir
D) Because the Companions agreed to narrate them

Key Takeaway
Prophetic reports spread inevitably due to their extraordinary nature, refuting the claim of isolated transmission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been silent about an extraordinary truth because you feared being alone in transmitting it? What does this passage say about your responsibility to speak when you witness something undeniable?
?
If you truly believed that an event was from Allah, would your tongue be able to stay silent? Reflect on a time you downplayed a miracle or blessing instead of spreading it.
?
The passage says truth is distinguished from falsehood in widespread reports. What fabrication about Islam are you silently accepting instead of exposing with the truth that has spread to you?

Prophethood

6 min
Divine Preservation and the Seal of Prophethood
Maturidi explains divine preservation of prophetic reports through signs and the seal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God preserves the prophetic message through the fear of kings, the distinctiveness of divine signs, and the final preservation in the Quran.

Core Idea
God preserves prophetic truth through overwhelming signs and seals prophethood with an incorruptible book.

Continuing his argument that prophetic reports are widely transmitted, Maturidi addresses the fear of kings and the sectarian disagreements of Jews and Christians. He then explains how God intervenes to revive the religion when it is altered, and finally seals prophethood with Muhammad (peace be upon him), preserving the message through the Quran. This lesson covers these divine mechanisms of preservation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the continuation of Maturidi's argument focusing on the kings and the preservation process.
2
Analyze the fear of kings
Maturidi notes that kings tried to extinguish the prophets' light out of fear for their kingdoms. Reflect on why this demonstrates the truth of prophethood.
The kings knew the prophets came from God despite their apparent weakness.
3
Contrast with Jewish and Christian consensus
Understand that the disagreements among Jews and Christians are about doctrinal matters, not about the divine signs themselves.
Their consensus is limited to their own followers.
4
Learn about divine preservation
Maturidi describes how God sends revivers (mujaddids) to restore the religion and finally preserves it through the Quran.
The Quran is preserved and remains until the end of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

God preserves His truth even when it is nearly erased. In your own life, have you ever felt that the truth of Islam has become faded or weak? What are you doing to actively revive and cling to it before God sends a reminder?
?
The Quran is preserved and cannot be altered. Yet have you altered the way you live with it—dismissing its commands, explaining them away to fit your desires? When will you open it to be truly changed by it?

The True Condition for Accepting Prophetic Reports
Maturidi refutes an objection and states the true condition for accepting prophetic reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the reliability of prophetic reports is determined not by the number of narrators but by the certainty and tranquility they produce in the heart.

Core Idea
Certainty from internal conviction, not numerical count, validates prophetic reports.

Maturidi addresses a common skeptical objection: prophetic proofs are transmitted through only one or two chains, which might seem to undermine their reliability. He calls this a severe calumny and instead points to the universal consensus of the Muslim community and the flawless character of the Prophet himself. The real standard, he argues, is the inner certainty and removal of doubts that these reports achieve, not mere quantity of narrators.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi immediately labels Al-Warraq's objection as a calumny.
2
Identify the two criteria
The passage contrasts two possible conditions for accepting reports: multitude of narrators versus 'capturing of hearts and tranquility.' Identify where each is mentioned.
Maturidi does not reject tawātur outright; he prioritizes internal certainty.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's example
Maturidi invokes the universal testimony of disbelievers who found no flaw in the Prophet. Consider how this strengthens the argument beyond mere numbers.
4
Synthesize the true condition
Conclude that the true condition is the soul's reassurance and the removal of misgivings. Even a few truthful narrators can produce certainty.
This aligns with the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسين الروندي طعن الوراق أخبار براهين الرسل من حيث وردت من طريق أو طريقين. وهذا بهت شديد، بل أجمعت عليها أمتنا . ثم أمر نبي الله مما توارث به الملحدون لتكلف الطعن والموحدون لرعاية الحق. مع تطابق الكفرة على أن يجدوا في خلقه ضعفاً أو في شجاعته أو له في شيء من المطامع رغبة، أو إلى شيء من فنون منافع الدنيا ميل ، فما وجدوا ذلك . فهذا لو كان شرط صحة الأخبار كثرة العدد، فكيف وشرطه الاستيلاء على القلوب وسكونها إليه، وطمأنينة النفس بالمخرج والفحوى ورفع ما يعترض من الظنون. وهكذا الأمر عند أخبار المحقين وإن قل عددهم.
Abu al-Husayn al-Rawandi said: Al-Warraq objected to the reports of the proofs of the prophets on the grounds that they came via one or two chains. This is a severe calumny; rather, our community has consensus upon them. Moreover, the affair of the Prophet of God is something that has been inherited by the atheists to strain in objection and the monotheists to observe the truth. The disbelievers concurred to find in his character any weakness, or in his courage, or any desire for some ambitions, or any inclination to some kinds of worldly benefits, but they found nothing of that. So if the condition for the soundness of reports were multitude of number, then how [could it be] when its condition is the capturing of hearts and their tranquility towards it, and the soul's reassurance through the result and content, and the removal of misgivings that arise. And such is the case with the reports of the truthful, even if their number is few.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Al-Warraq objects that the proofs of the prophets are transmitted via only one or two chains, implying they are unreliable. Maturidi responds by calling this a severe calumny, noting that the entire Muslim community has consensus on their truth. He then points to the Prophet Muhammad (pbuh): his character was scrutinized by disbelievers seeking any flaw, but they found none. This universal testimony outweighs numerical criteria. Maturidi then states the real condition for accepting such reports: it is not the quantity of narrators but the impact on hearts—that the report induces certainty and tranquility, removing doubts. Thus, even if the number of narrators is small, the report of the truthful is authoritative.

Key Terms
بهت (calumny)
أجمعت (consensus)
الاستيلاء على القلوب (capturing hearts)
طمأنينة النفس (reassurance of soul)
ظنون (misgivings)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the true condition for the soundness of prophetic reports?
A) They must be transmitted by at least ten companions
B) They must capture hearts and produce tranquility
C) They must be written in the Quran
D) They must be agreed upon by all Muslims unanimously

Key Takeaway
The soundness of prophetic reports depends on the certainty and tranquility they produce in the heart, not on the number of chains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a prophetic report you believe in. Is your belief rooted in the number of narrators or in the inner certainty and tranquility it produces? How do you know the difference?
?
The disbelievers examined the Prophet and found no fault. Have you ever examined your own attachment to his teachings with similar honesty? What did you uncover?
?
If the true condition for truth is capturing hearts, has your heart been truly captured by the prophetic message? If not, what barrier remains, and what will you do about it today?

Answering the Objection: 'Ask the People of Remembrance'
Maturidi enumerates three responses to an objection against a Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the objection that the Quran commands consulting those who conceal the truth, using three distinct lines of reasoning.

Core Idea
Even when people conceal truth, God can compel them to witness, making it a sign.

Al-Warraq raises a sharp objection: if the People of the Book are accused of hiding the truth, why does the Quran command asking them? Maturidi offers three insightful answers that reveal the depth of Quranic argumentation. In this lesson, we explore these responses and the logic behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the objection and the three answers. Let the structure become clear.
The passage begins with the objection, then 'So it was answered' introduces the first answer, then 'Also' and 'And the third' introduce the other two.
2
Identify the three answers
List the three answers Maturidi gives. Each has a different focus: divine compulsion, overcoming obstinacy, and restricting to converts.
3
Examine the first answer
Understand that after clear proofs, God compelled them to acknowledge the truth, making their testimony a sign. This is supported by a similar Quranic verse about scholars of Israel.
The key phrase is 'God compels them' (يسخرهم).
4
Examine the second answer
Recognize that sometimes a person is obstinate even after proof. Telling them to ask a trusted individual can help remove obstinacy.
The term 'لجاج' (obstinacy) is important.
5
Examine the third answer
The command may refer specifically to those who have already accepted Islam among them.
This narrows the scope of the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الوراق في قوله فاسألوا أهل الذكر ﴾ الآية، أن كيف أمر بذلك مع الشهادة عليهم بكتمان الحق؟ فأجيب بما إذ أيد الله نبوة محمد بالحجج القاهرة مالوا إلى الكتاب؛ فقيل لهم ذلك على أن الله يُسخرهم في ذلك ويضطرهم إلى الموافقة؛ فيكون ذلك من جليل آياته إذ جمع عليه الأعداء والأولياء، وهو كقوله لم يكن لهم آية أن يعلمه علماء بني إسرائيل. وأيضاً إن ذا على ما يعرف من لجاج الرجل بعد إقامة البرهان عليه أن يقال : فاسأل ذلك فلانا ممن يطمع سكون قلبه إليه فيترك اللجاج. والثالث أن يكون المراد يرجع إلى من أسلم منهم. وبالله التوفيق.
And al-Warraq objected to His saying: 'Ask the people of remembrance'—the verse—how is that commanded while witness is against them that they conceal the truth? So it was answered: Since God supported the prophethood of Muhammad with overwhelming proofs, they inclined to the Book; so that was said to them because God compels them in that and forces them to agree; so that becomes among His great signs when He gathered against it the enemies and the friends, and it is like His saying: 'It is not a sign for them that the scholars of the Children of Israel know him?' Also, this is in accord with what is known of a man's obstinacy after the proof is established upon him, that it is said: 'Ask that so-and-so from whom he hopes his heart will settle so he abandons obstinacy.' And the third is that the intent refers to those who accepted Islam among them. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and three answers. The critic Al-Warraq objects to the Quranic verse 'Ask the people of the Reminder' (i.e., the People of the Book), pointing out that these people are accused of concealing truth, so how can one be commanded to ask them? Maturidi provides three responses. First: After God supported Muhammad with overwhelming proofs, the People of the Book inclined to acknowledge the truth, and God compelled them to testify, so this becomes a sign when enemies and friends are united. This is similar to the verse about the scholars of Israel knowing the Prophet. Second: Sometimes a person is obstinate even after proof; telling him to ask someone whose testimony he trusts helps remove obstinacy. Third: The verse may refer to those who have already accepted Islam from among them. Thus, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
أهل الذكر (people of remembrance)
بالحجج القاهرة (with overwhelming proofs)
يسخرهم (compels them)
لجاج (obstinacy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse commands Muslims to seek religious knowledge from any non-Muslim without restriction.
Correction: Maturidi's answers show the command was either for those compelled by God, as a method to overcome obstinacy, or for those who had already converted. It does not grant blanket authority to consult non-Muslims.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the answers given to the objection about the verse 'Ask the people of remembrance'?
A) God compelled them after clear proofs so their testimony becomes a sign
B) The command is only for those who have already converted to Islam
C) The People of the Book are trustworthy in all matters
D) Asking a specific individual can remove obstinacy in an opponent

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes al-Warraq's objection by showing that the verse either refers to compelled witnesses, a way to overcome obstinacy, or to those who had already embraced Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse that seems difficult to reconcile, do you immediately assume contradiction, or do you seek the deeper explanations as Maturidi did? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom?
?
Think of a time you were obstinate about a truth that was clear to you. Who could you have asked to settle your heart? How can you lower your pride next time?
?
Have you ever felt Allah compelling you to acknowledge a truth you were avoiding? How did that moment of forced recognition change your relationship with Him?

The Condition for Accepting Reports: Tranquility over Numbers
Maturidi refutes al-Warraq's objection and states the true condition for report validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the true criterion for accepting reports is not numerical multiplicity but the tranquility and certainty they produce in the heart.

Core Idea
The validity of reports rests on tranquility, not on numbers.

In this passage, Maturidi confronts an objection from al-Warraq that the miraculous proofs of the messengers were transmitted through only one or two chains. He responds by shifting the criterion from quantity of transmitters to the quality of conviction. The lesson will walk through his refutation and his positive statement of the true condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very direct and forceful style here.
2
Identify the objection and rebuttal
Find al-Warraq's objection in the first line. Then see how Maturidi responds: he calls it 'outrageous slander' and invokes community consensus and the Prophet's character.
The rebuttal has three parts: strong condemnation, appeal to consensus, and empirical evidence.
3
Understand the conditional argument
Read the sentence beginning with 'If the condition...'. This is a crucial shift from numbers to tranquility. Ask yourself: why does Maturidi think numbers are insufficient?
The condition is defined as 'gaining control over hearts' and 'tranquility of the soul'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسين الروندي طعن الوراق أخبار براهين الرسل من حيث وردت من طريق أو طريقين. وهذا بهت شديد، بل أجمعت عليها أمتنا. ثم أمر نبي الله مما توارث به الملحدون لتكلف الطعن والموحدون لرعاية الحق. مع تطابق الكفرة على أن يجدوا في خلقه ضعفا أو في شجاعته أو له في شيء من المطامع رغبة، أو إلى شيء من فنون منافع الدنيا ميل، فما وجدوا ذلك. فهذا لو كان شرط صحة الأخبار كثرة العدد، فكيف وشرطه الاستيلاء على القلوب وسكونها إليه، وطمأنينة النفس بالمخرج والفحوى ورفع ما يعترض من الظنون. وهكذا الأمر عند أخبار المحقين وإن قل عددهم.
Abu al-Husayn al-Rawandi said: al-Warraq attacked the news of the proofs of the messengers on the basis that they came through one or two chains. This is an outrageous slander. And such is the case with the reports of the truthful even if their number is few.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection by al-Warraq against the transmission of miraculous proofs of the messengers due to few chains. Maturidi calls it slander and asserts that the Muslim community has agreed upon those reports. He then notes that the Prophet's character was examined by both atheists and disbelievers seeking faults, but none found any. He argues that if the criterion for accepting reports were large numbers, then it would fail, but the actual criterion is gaining mastery over hearts, causing tranquility, and removing doubts. This applies to reports of truthful people even if few.

Correction: Maturidi does not discard multiplicity entirely; he redefines the essential condition as causing certainty (tranquility), which numbers alone do not guarantee.
