Maturidi's Three Answers to the Objection on 'Ask the People of Remembrance'
Maturidi refutes al-Warraq's objection with three answers and two further possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the objection that the Quranic command to ask the People of the Book is undermined by their concealment of truth, through three distinct answers and additional possibilities.

Core Idea
God's command to ask remains valid; He can compel testimony or address specific believers.

Al-Warraq raised a critical objection: if the People of the Book are known to conceal the truth, why does Allah command asking them? Imam Maturidi responds with a multi-layered defense, showing that the command is not based on their goodwill but on divine coercion, human psychology, or the specific context of those who believed. This passage demonstrates Maturidi's skill in harmonizing Quranic commands with apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Read the passage and identify al-Warraq's objection: how can Allah command asking the People of the Book when they are known to conceal the truth? Notice that this objection targets the apparent inconsistency in the Quran.
The objection is based on the testimony against them (الشهادة عليهم بكتمان الحق).
2
First Answer: Divine Compulsion
Examine the first answer: when Allah supported the Prophet with overwhelming proofs, the People of the Book inclined to the Book. Allah forced them to agree, making their testimony a great sign. Consider how this answer turns the objection into a proof of prophethood.
Compare with Quran 26:197 about the scholars of Israel knowing it.
3
Second Answer: Addressing Obstinacy
Study the second answer: after establishing proof against a stubborn person, he may be told to ask someone he trusts to calm his heart and abandon obstinacy. This shows the command is psychological, not requiring impartiality.
Understand the term 'لجاج' (obstinacy) and how the command targets that trait.
4
Third Answer and Additional Possibilities
Review the third answer: the command may refer to those among the People of the Book who had embraced Islam. Then note the two additional possibilities: some may secretly admit the truth, or 'people of remembrance' could mean honorable people who avoid lying. Appreciate the comprehensive nature of the defense.
Maturidi concludes with 'والله أعلم' (God knows best), showing humility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الوراق في قوله فاسألوا أهل الذكر [النحل، 43/16؛ الأنبياء، 7/21] الآية، أن كيف أمر بذلك مع الشهادة عليهم بكتمان الحق؟ فأجيب بما إذ أيد الله نبوة محمد بالحجج القاهرة مالوا إلى الكتاب؛ فقيل لهم ذلك على أن الله يسخرهم في ذلك ويضطرهم إلى الموافقة؛ فيكون ذلك من جليل آياته إذ جمع عليه الأعداء والأولياء، وهو كقوله لم يكن لهم آية أن يعلمه علماء بني إسرائيل [الشعراء، 197/26]. وأيضا إن ذا على ما يعرف من لجاج الرجل بعد إقامة البرهان عليه أن يقال: فاسأل ذلك فلانا ممن يطمع سكون قلبه إليه فيترك اللجاج. والثالث أن يكون المراد يرجع إلى من أسلم منهم. وبالله التوفيق. وجائز أن يكون في قوم يقرون بذلك سرا كقوله: أتأمرون الناس بالبر [البقرة، 44/2] الآية. وجائز أن يكون المراد بأهل الذكر هم أهل الشرف الذين يمنعهم شرفهم عند التحكيم إليهم عن الكذب. والله أعلم.
And al-Warraq attacked His saying: 'Ask the people of remembrance' [Quran 16:43; 21:7], the verse, saying: How can He command that despite the testimony against them that they conceal the truth? So it was answered: When God supported the prophethood of Muhammad with overwhelming proofs, they inclined to the Book. So that was said to them because God forces them in that and compels them to agreement, so that becomes one of His great signs when He gathers enemies and allies against it. It is like His saying: 'It was not a sign for them that the scholars of the Children of Israel know it' [Quran 26:197]. Also, this is based on what is known of a man's obstinacy after the proof is established against him; it is said: Ask that so-and-so from whom he hopes his heart will calm down, so he leaves obstinacy. Third: It may mean that the address refers to those among them who had embraced Islam. And with God is success. And it is possible that there are people who admit that secretly, as in His saying: 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon people' [Quran 2:44] the verse. And it is possible that 'people of remembrance' means people of honor whose honor prevents them from lying when referred to for arbitration. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage refutes al-Warraq's objection to the Quranic command to ask the People of the Book despite their known concealment of truth. Three main answers are given: First, when God supported Muhammad with overwhelming proofs, they inclined to the Book, so God forces them to agree, turning their testimony into a sign. Second, a stubborn person may be told to ask someone he trusts to cease obstinacy. Third, it may refer to those who had embraced Islam. Then two additional possibilities are added: the people may admit secretly, or 'people of remembrance' refers to honorable people who avoid lying. The passage concludes with 'God knows best.'

الشهادة عليهم بكتمان الحق
الحجج القاهرة
اللجاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command to ask the People of the Book is invalid because they conceal the truth.
Correction: Maturidi shows the command remains valid through divine compulsion, addressing obstinacy, or referring to believers among them.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the Qur'anic command remains rational through divine compulsion, human psychology, and contextual interpretation.

Angels at Badr but Not at Uhud: Two Answers
Maturidi answers objection about angels at Badr vs Uhud with two responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the absence of angels at Uhud does not disprove their presence at Badr, and learn two responses to this objection.

Core Idea
Angels appeared at Badr but not Uhud because each battle served a different divine purpose.

Al-Warraq raised a logical objection: if angels helped at Badr, why not at Uhud? Maturidi offers two compelling answers that reveal the wisdom behind divine support. This passage shows how theological objections can be answered by considering context and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening where al-Warraq attacks the report of angels at Badr by asking where they were at Uhud. See how this objection works: if a pattern of angelic help existed, it should be consistent.
Al-Warraq assumes that if angels help in one battle, they must help in all similar battles.
2
Examine the first answer
Maturidi's first answer points to physical evidence: heads appeared at Badr without a visible killer, and enemies reported seeing unrecognizable forms. This suggests angelic intervention was observable.
This answer relies on testimonial evidence from the battle itself.
3
Examine the second answer
The second answer focuses on purpose: Badr was the first war, and God wanted to support the Muslims to make truth manifest and falsehood null. After that, the need for visible angelic support diminished.
This answer highlights that divine help is tailored to specific needs and times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الوراق إخبار رسول الله بحضور الملائكة يوم بدر، قال: أين كانوا يوم أحد؟ جواب الأول ظهور رؤوس ببدر بلا قاتل رأوه، وبيان المذكور من الأعداء أنهم رأوا صورا لم يعرفوهم. وجواب الثاني أن ذلك أول حرب، فأراد الله تعالى أن ينصرهم ليظهر الحق ويبطل الباطل.
And al-Warraq attacked the report of the Messenger of God about the presence of the angels on the day of Badr. He said: Where were they on the day of Uhud? The first answer: The appearance of heads at Badr without a killer they saw, and the statement of the mentioned enemies that they saw forms they did not recognize. The second answer: That was the first battle, so God Almighty wanted to support them to make the truth manifest and falsehood null.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage addresses al-Warraq's objection: if angels came to help at Badr, why did they not appear at Uhud? Two answers are given. First, at Badr, heads appeared without an identifiable killer, and enemies reported seeing unrecognizable forms, indicating angelic involvement. Second, Badr was the first battle, so God supported the Muslims to establish truth and abolish falsehood. The implication is that after the truth was manifest, the need for visible angelic support diminished.

Key Terms
حضور الملائكة
يوم بدر
يوم أحد
القهر
الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of angels at Uhud disproves their presence at Badr.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the two battles had different circumstances: at Badr there was observable evidence, and it was the first war requiring divine support to establish truth.

Checkpoint
What is one answer given for the absence of angels at Uhud?
A) The angels were busy elsewhere.
B) The Muslims were not in need.
C) Badr was the first war and God wanted to support them to manifest truth.
D) The angels only appear in battles with large numbers.

Key Takeaway
Angelic help at Badr but not at Uhud is explained by observable evidence and the unique purpose of the first battle to establish truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a 'first battle' in your life—a moment where truth needs to be established—do you truly trust that God will support you, even if you cannot see His help? What would change in your actions if you believed that help is assured?
?
The first answer points to observable evidence of angelic involvement. In your own life, are you paying attention to the small signs of God's support that others might dismiss, or are you only looking for dramatic interventions? What might you be missing?
?
God supported the Muslims to manifest truth and nullify falsehood. How committed are you to standing for truth when it costs you, like it cost the Muslims at Badr? Identify one situation this week where you can visibly uphold truth, and ask God to support you in it.

Signs of Prophethood in Badr
Maturidi lists signs from Badr: dust hitting each, mubahala, and enemy gathering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three miraculous signs from the Battle of Badr that Maturidi presents as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
The Battle of Badr contained multiple miraculous signs pointing to the truth of the Prophet.

Maturidi draws attention to specific events in the Battle of Badr that serve as signs for those who reflect. Among these are the miraculous dust that struck every enemy, an imprecation that backfired on its utterer, and the gathering of polytheist leaders. This brief passage invites us to consider how even small details in history can carry profound theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of Maturidi.
2
Identify the three signs
List the three aspects Maturidi mentions. They are not explicitly numbered but are distinct.
3
Reflect on how each sign demonstrates prophecy
For each sign, ask: How does this event point to the truth of the Prophet's mission? Consider the miraculous nature of the dust, the irony of Abu Jahl's prayer, and the significance of the leaders' gathering.
4
Note the eloquence of Abu Jahl's statement
Maturidi says Abu Jahl's statement 'resembles mubahala'—an imprecation where each side calls on God to curse the liar. Reflect on how the enemy's own words became evidence against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: وفي أمر بدر وجوه من المعتبر. أحدها عمل كف من تراب أن أصاب كلا منهم؛ وفيه ما ذكر؛ وفيه ما يشبه المباهلة من قول أبي جهل: 'اللهم انصر أبرنا وأوصلنا للرحم'، وجمع الأئمة من الكفرة وغير ذلك. والله الموفق.
The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: In the matter of Badr there are aspects to consider. One of them: the action of a handful of dust that hit each of them; and in it what was mentioned; and in it what resembles the mubahala (imprecation) from the saying of Abu Jahl: 'O God, support the most righteous of us and the one who maintains family ties,' and the gathering of the leaders of the disbelievers, and other things. And God is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage lists several notable signs from the Battle of Badr that serve as evidence. The first point is that a handful of dust thrown by the Prophet hit each enemy, a miraculous event. Second, there is the mention of the mubahala-like imprecation of Abu Jahl, who called on God to support the most righteous and the one who maintains family ties, ironically against himself. Third is the gathering of the leaders of the disbelievers. These are considered aspects for reflection, reinforcing the truth of prophethood.

Defending the Report of Angels at Badr
Maturidi gives two answers to al-Warraq's objection about angels at Badr and Uhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi defends the prophetic report of angels at Badr against al-Warraq's objection by providing two distinct rational answers.

Core Idea
Allah's help varies by divine wisdom, not by human expectation.

Al-Warraq challenges a prophetic report: if angels were present at Badr, why were they absent at Uhud? This objection might seem to undermine the credibility of the report. Maturidi responds with two reasoned answers that show the divine wisdom behind the different manifestations of divine aid. Let's examine his argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Warraq's objection
Read the passage to grasp al-Warraq's challenge: he uses the absence of angels at Uhud to question the report of their presence at Badr. Why might this be a powerful objection?
The objection assumes that if angels always help believers in battle, they should appear in every battle.
2
Examine Maturidi's first answer
The first answer focuses on the physical evidence at Badr: heads appeared without any visible human fighter. This suggests angelic involvement. Learn how Maturidi uses this to counter the objection.
3
Examine Maturidi's second answer
The second answer places the event in context: Badr was the first battle, so Allah intended a clear sign to establish truth. The absence at Uhud does not negate the special nature of Badr.
This answer highlights the principle that Allah's aid is situational and purposeful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الورّاق إخبار رسول الله بحضور الملائكة يوم بدر ، قال : أين كانوا يوم أحد؟ جواب الأول ظهور روؤس ببدر بلا قاتل رأوه ، وبيان المذكور من الأعداء أنهم رأوا صورا لم يعرفوهم . وجواب الثاني أن ذلك أول حرب، فأراد الله تعالى أن ينصرهم ليظهر الحق ويبطل الباطل.
And al-Warraq objected to the report of the Messenger of Allah about the presence of angels on the day of Badr. He said: 'Where were they on the day of Uhud?' The first answer: [At Badr] heads appeared without a fighter they saw, and the mentioned enemies saw forms they did not recognize. The second answer: That was the first battle, so Allah intended to give them victory to manifest the truth and nullify falsehood.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage records a challenge from a figure named al-Warraq regarding the prophetic report that angels were present at the Battle of Badr. Al-Warraq argues, 'If angels were present at Badr, why were they not present at Uhud?' Maturidi provides two answers. The first answer is that at Badr, the heads of the disbelievers were struck down by unseen fighters (angels), and the enemies saw forms they did not recognize as human. The second answer is that Badr was the first battle, so Allah specially aided the Muslims to establish the truth and defeat falsehood, as a clear sign. The lesson shows that Allah's aid can vary according to divine wisdom, and the absence of angels at Uhud does not disprove their presence at Badr.

Key Terms
الملائكة
بدر
أحد
الورّاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If angels were present at Badr, they must always be present in battles to help Muslims.
Correction: Maturidi shows that Allah's help is given according to divine wisdom and context; the special sign at Badr does not imply perpetual angelic presence in every battle.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi answer al-Warraq's objection about the absence of angels at Uhud?
A) He says the angels were present but unseen
B) He gives two answers: heads appeared without visible fighters, and Badr was the first battle so Allah wanted a clear sign
C) He says the report about angels at Badr is not authentic
D) He says the angels were sent only to Badr due to the large number of disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Maturidi defends the report of angels at Badr by providing both empirical evidence and contextual wisdom, demonstrating that divine aid is not uniform but purposeful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt abandoned by Allah because a specific prayer for help went unanswered? How does Maturidi's explanation about the absence of angels at Uhud challenge your assumption that divine help must always appear in the same spectacular way?
?
When you face a trial and do not see the immediate or visible support you hoped for, do you begin to doubt that Allah is with you? What would it take for you to trust His wisdom, even when His help seems absent or delayed, as at Uhud?
?
Are you willing to accept that Allah's help may be invisible or come in a form you do not recognize, while still holding firmly to His promise? What concrete step can you take this week to surrender your expectations to His wisdom, rather than demanding a sign like the companions saw at Badr?

Proof of Prophethood through the Prophet's Perfection
Maturidi presents proofs of Muhammad's prophethood through his physical and moral perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's physical and moral perfection serve as proof of his prophethood according to Imam Maturidi.

Core Idea
The Prophet's flawless nature is itself a divine sign of his prophethood.

Imam Maturidi begins by stating that prophethood is established through multiple lines of evidence, including the very substance (jawhar) of the prophet. He then focuses on the Prophet Muhammad's physical beauty and moral excellence as compelling proofs. This passage invites us to see the Prophet's perfection not merely as admirable qualities but as clear indicators of his divine mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three categories of proof
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Maturidi lists three proofs: substance, signs, and circumstances. Focus on the first proof, which is the main subject.
The passage initially mentions all three but then elaborates only on jawhar.
2
List the physical attributes of the Prophet mentioned
Identify the descriptions of the Prophet's physical perfection: his face more beautiful than the moon, fragrance sweeter than musk, body softer than silk, and his sweat used as perfume. Recognise that these are extraordinary traits.
These attributes are not ordinary human qualities; they indicate a special creation.
3
List the moral attributes mentioned
Note the Prophet's moral perfections: no lies, no missteps, no flight from enemies, no evil character, no obscenity, no self-vengeance, and extreme compassion. Also note the Quranic references to his grief for his people.
The moral perfection complements the physical to form a complete proof.
4
Reflect on why these traits prove prophethood
Ask yourself: Why does freedom from defects and adornment with every beauty indicate the highest station? Because such completeness cannot be achieved by human effort; it is a gift from God, marking the Prophet as His chosen messenger.
This understanding guards against reducing prophethood to miracles alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أنها تثبت بالجوهر، ثم بآيات حسية وعقلية، ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه. فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه، وأنه كان أطيب ريحا من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ بعرقه فينقع به في الطيب. وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالا؛ وجل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذي آفات في الخلقة. فدل براءته عن كل الآفات وزينه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار. ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ولا في أخلاقه سوء. بل كان على ما وصف لا يدارى ولا يمارى، ولا يعرف منه فحش، ولا ينتصر لنفسه. وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله: فلا تذهب نفسك عليهم حسرات [فاطر، ٨/٣٥]، وقوله: لعلك باخع نفسك، الآية؛ وفي التحزن بما فيه هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله وعصمه بقوله:
Then the discourse on the prophethood of the prophets, and specifically on the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, that it is established by the substance (jawhar), then by sensory and rational signs, then by the correspondence of the appearance of circumstances that are circumstances of need for him. As for the matter of substance, we have explained its beginning along with what was mentioned regarding it: that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and that he was sweeter in fragrance than musk and softer than silk; and his sweat was taken and soaked in perfume. And his creation was described with such beauty and handsomeness that no one is known to be described with the like; and the eye sees that it is stirred in perplexity by one with defects in creation. So his being free from all defects and his adornment with every adornment indicates his deserving the highest ranks in creation and the best of destinies. And that is indicated by the fact that no lie was ever taken from him, no misstep was known from him, no flight from his enemies, and no evil in his character. Rather, he was as described: not vied with nor disputed, and no obscenity was known from him, and he did not avenge himself. And he was in compassion to the degree that he was reproached for it in His saying: 'So do not let yourself be consumed in grief over them' [Fatir, 35:8], and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself' [al-Shu'ara, 26:3], the verse; and in grief to the point of perishing of creation as God described him and protected him by His saying: ...
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalāʾil) of prophethood, specifically for Muhammad (saw). Maturidi states that prophethood is established by three things: (1) the substance (jawhar) of the prophet—his personal nature and physical perfection; (2) sensory and rational signs (āyāt ḥissiyya wa ʿaqliyya); (3) the correspondence of the circumstances of his time (the need for a prophet). He then elaborates on the first proof—the substance of the Prophet. He describes his physical beauty: his face was more beautiful than the full moon, his fragrance sweeter than musk, his body softer than silk, and his sweat was used as perfume. No one has ever been described with such beauty. This freedom from physical defects and his adornment with every beauty indicate that he deserves the highest station in creation. He then adds moral perfection: no lie, no fault, no fleeing from enemies, no evil character. He never engaged in obscenity or sought revenge. His compassion was so profound that God reproached him for excessive grief over disbelievers, as in Qur'anic verses. This combination of physical and moral perfection serves as a clear sign (dalīl) of his prophethood, because such a complete nature cannot be attained by ordinary humans; it is a gift from God, marking him as a messenger.

Key Terms
إثبات النبوة
الجوهر
آيات حسية
آيات عقلية
حسن الخلق
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood is proven only by miracles.
Correction: Maturidi includes the personal perfection of the prophet as a key proof, showing that the prophet's very nature and character are signs from God.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi mean by 'established by the substance (jawhar)' in proving the Prophet's message?
A) That the Prophet had a physical body made of a special substance.
B) That the Prophet's physical and moral perfection are signs of his prophethood.
C) That the Prophet's substance was the first creation.
D) That the Prophet's message is proven by the substance of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's physical and moral perfection, being unmatched and flawless, serve as a clear proof of his prophethood because such completeness can only come from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's compassion was so extreme that Allah rebuked him for his grief over disbelievers. When was the last time your concern for others was so deep that it drove you to self-sacrifice? Do you truly love people as he did, or is your love conditional?
?
If the Prophet's physical and moral perfection is a divine sign, what does your own imperfection—your lies, your faults, your pride—say about your distance from that model? Will you let his perfection judge you or guide you?
?
You recite the shahada, but do you actually believe that Muhammad's flawless nature is a proof from God? If yes, why do you still hesitate to obey him in the areas of your life where you know you are deficient? What is holding you back from surrender?

Proof of Prophethood through Essential Perfection
Maturidi enumerates the proofs of prophethood and elaborates on the proof from essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Prophet's physical and spiritual perfection as a primary proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's essence is the first proof of his prophethood.

Maturidi begins his proof of Muhammad's prophethood by examining the very essence of the Prophet. He argues that the perfection of his creation, free from defects, points directly to his divine selection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the descriptions of the Prophet's appearance and scent.
2
Identify the argument
Notice how Maturidi contrasts the Prophet's perfection with the defects seen in others to argue for his elevated status.
3
Reflect on the implication
Understand why freedom from defects is considered evidence of prophethood in this framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات رسالة محمد. ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أنها تثبت بالجوهر، ثم بآيات حسية وعقلية، ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه. فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه، وأنه كان أطيب ريحاً من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ بعَرَقِه فيُنقع به في الطيب. وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يُعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالاً؛ وجُل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذي آفات في الخلقة. فدل براءته عن كل الآفات وزَيَّنه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار. ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ولا في أخلاقه سوء. بل كان على ما وصف لا يُدارى ولا يمارى، ولا يعرف منه فُحش، ولا ينتصر لنفسه. وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله: فلا تذهب نفسك عليهم حسرات، وقوله: لعلك باخع نفسك، الآية؛ وفي التحزن بما فيه هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله وعصمه بقوله: ولا تحزن عليهم، وقال: عزيز عليه ما عنتم، الآية. وكان بالكرم بحيث عوتب بقوله: ولا تبسطها كل البسط. وقيل: لم يكن يدخر شيئًا لغد. وقد عُرض عليه أعلى ما يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بان يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب فيه، بل عادى الله الأقوياء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله بالرعب في قلوب الخلق فلم يكن يقصد إليهم في الحرب إلا خافوه. وقيل له: والله يعصمك من الناس، فلم يَخَفّهم بعد ذلك، ولا ذُكر أنه ولاهم دبره، على ما أصاب أتباعه النكبات والشدائد ووعد أن يبلغ مُلك أمته ما زُوي له من الأرض من المشارق والمغارب، وما روى عما ذكر من أنواع الفزع في قلوب أعدائه
Establishment of the message of Muhammad. Then the statement concerning the prophethood of the prophets, and especially concerning the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace: that it is established by the essence, then by sensory and intellectual signs, then by the agreement of the emergence of circumstances which are circumstances of need for him. As for the matter of the essence, we have already explained its beginning with what was mentioned concerning it: that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and that he was more fragrant than musk and softer than silk, and his sweat would be taken and soaked in perfume. And his creation was described in a way that no one is known to have been described with similar handsomeness and beauty; while the eye sees most people agitated in confusion with defects in their creation. So his freedom from all defects and his adornment with every adornment indicated his deserving the highest ranks in creation and the best capacities. And that is indicated by the fact that no lie was ever attributed to him, nor was any slip known from him, nor any flight from his enemies, nor any evil in his character. Rather, he was as described: he would not be vied with nor disputed, nor was obscenity known from him, nor would he avenge himself. And he was in compassion to the degree that he was reproached for it in His saying: 'So do not let your soul be consumed in regret over them' (Fatir 35:8), and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself' (ash-Shu'ara 26:3), the verse; and in sorrow to the extent of the destruction of creation, as God described him and protected him with His saying: 'And do not grieve over them' (an-Nahl 16:127), and He said: 'Grievous to him is what you suffer' (at-Tawbah 9:128), the verse. And he was in generosity to the extent that he was reproached with His saying: 'And do not stretch it forth completely' (al-Isra 17:29). And it was said: He would not save anything for tomorrow. And the highest of worldly goods and leadership were offered to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond; rather, he opposed the powerful, the kings, and the chiefs of God until God honored him with fear in the hearts of creation, so that whenever he set out against them in war they feared him. And it was said to him: 'God will protect you from the people' (al-Ma'ida 5:67), so he did not fear them after that, nor is it mentioned that he turned his back to them, despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships, and he promised that the dominion of his community would reach what was folded for him of the earth from east to west, and what has been narrated concerning the types of terror in the hearts of his enemies.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) based on his essential perfection and moral character. The author begins by stating that prophethood is established through three things: the essence (al-jawhar), sensory and intellectual signs, and the agreement of the circumstances of need. He then focuses on the first proof: the essence. This refers to the Prophet's physical and spiritual perfection as inherent in his person. He mentions that the Prophet's face was more beautiful than the full moon, his scent was sweeter than musk, his body softer than silk, and his sweat was used in perfume. His description surpasses any known human perfection. The author argues that freedom from all defects and adornment with every virtue prove that he deserves the highest rank in creation and the best capacities. Additional evidence is that no lie or slip was ever known from him; he never fled from enemies nor had any evil in his character. He was not contentious, never used obscenity, and did not seek revenge for himself. His compassion was so great that God reproached him for excessive grief over his people, quoting verses such as 'So do not let your soul be consumed in regret over them' (35:8) and 'Perhaps you would kill yourself' (26:3). God consoled him with 'Do not grieve over them' (16:127) and praised his mercy in 'Grievous to him is what you suffer' (9:128). His generosity was such that he was instructed not to be extravagant (17:29), and he never saved anything for tomorrow. When offered worldly wealth and leadership in exchange for compromise, he refused and opposed the powerful and the kings. God granted him victory through fear instilled in enemies, and he was assured of divine protection (5:67), so he never feared them. Despite the hardships faced by his followers, he promised that the dominion of his community would extend from east to west. The passage closes by referring to the fear in the hearts of his enemies.

Key Terms
جوهر
نبوة
آيات حسية وعقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof of prophethood relies solely on miracles.
Correction: Maturidi emphasizes the inherent perfection of the Prophet's being as a primary evidence, arguing that his essence itself indicates his divine selection.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the three proofs of Muhammad's prophethood?
A) The essence
B) Sensory and intellectual signs
C) The agreement of circumstances of need
D) The miracles of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's physical and spiritual perfection, free from defects, is itself a proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the Prophet’s essence—his beauty, fragrance, and freedom from defects—is itself a proof of his prophethood. Do you truly feel the weight of that perfection in your heart, or has it become just a fact you acknowledge? What one change in your daily devotion would show that you are moved by his perfection?
?
The passage says the Prophet was adorned with every adornment and free from every defect. Think of one area of your character where you have become comfortable with a defect (e.g., a bad habit, a lack of patience). How does the Prophet’s perfection challenge you to abandon that defect starting today?
?
This proof does not rely on a miracle you cannot see but on the Prophet’s very being. If his essence is enough to prove his prophethood, why do you still seek signs in your own life before fully committing to his way? What step of trust can you take this week based solely on the truth of his prophethood as shown by his person?

Proof through Perfect Moral Character
Maturidi lists exemplary character traits as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Prophet's moral character, including truthfulness, compassion, generosity, and courage, as evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character is a living proof of his prophethood.

After establishing the proof through essence, Maturidi turns to the Prophet's character. He argues that a person of such perfect morality, without any fault, must be a true prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify character traits
As you read, list the specific character traits Maturidi attributes to the Prophet (e.g., no lie, compassion, generosity).
2
Notice the scriptural references
Observe how Maturidi supports his claims with Quranic verses that show God's approval or reproach.
3
Understand the argument
Realize that the consistency and perfection of character, even in the face of trials, point to divine guidance.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why such character evidence is compelling in the Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات رسالة محمد. ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أنها تثبت بالجوهر، ثم بآيات حسية وعقلية، ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه. فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه، وأنه كان أطيب ريحاً من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ بعَرَقِه فيُنقع به في الطيب. وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يُعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالاً؛ وجُل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذي آفات في الخلقة. فدل براءته عن كل الآفات وزَيَّنه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار. ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ولا في أخلاقه سوء. بل كان على ما وصف لا يُدارى ولا يمارى، ولا يعرف منه فُحش، ولا ينتصر لنفسه. وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله: فلا تذهب نفسك عليهم حسرات، وقوله: لعلك باخع نفسك، الآية؛ وفي التحزن بما فيه هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله وعصمه بقوله: ولا تحزن عليهم، وقال: عزيز عليه ما عنتم، الآية. وكان بالكرم بحيث عوتب بقوله: ولا تبسطها كل البسط. وقيل: لم يكن يدخر شيئًا لغد. وقد عُرض عليه أعلى ما يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بان يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب فيه، بل عادى الله الأقوياء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله بالرعب في قلوب الخلق فلم يكن يقصد إليهم في الحرب إلا خافوه. وقيل له: والله يعصمك من الناس، فلم يَخَفّهم بعد ذلك، ولا ذُكر أنه ولاهم دبره، على ما أصاب أتباعه النكبات والشدائد ووعد أن يبلغ مُلك أمته ما زُوي له من الأرض من المشارق والمغارب، وما روى عما ذكر من أنواع الفزع في قلوب أعدائه
Establishment of the message of Muhammad. Then the statement concerning the prophethood of the prophets, and especially concerning the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace: that it is established by the essence, then by sensory and intellectual signs, then by the agreement of the emergence of circumstances which are circumstances of need for him. As for the matter of the essence, we have already explained its beginning with what was mentioned concerning it: that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and that he was more fragrant than musk and softer than silk, and his sweat would be taken and soaked in perfume. And his creation was described in a way that no one is known to have been described with similar handsomeness and beauty; while the eye sees most people agitated in confusion with defects in their creation. So his freedom from all defects and his adornment with every adornment indicated his deserving the highest ranks in creation and the best capacities. And that is indicated by the fact that no lie was ever attributed to him, nor was any slip known from him, nor any flight from his enemies, nor any evil in his character. Rather, he was as described: he would not be vied with nor disputed, nor was obscenity known from him, nor would he avenge himself. And he was in compassion to the degree that he was reproached for it in His saying: 'So do not let your soul be consumed in regret over them' (Fatir 35:8), and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself' (ash-Shu'ara 26:3), the verse; and in sorrow to the extent of the destruction of creation, as God described him and protected him with His saying: 'And do not grieve over them' (an-Nahl 16:127), and He said: 'Grievous to him is what you suffer' (at-Tawbah 9:128), the verse. And he was in generosity to the extent that he was reproached with His saying: 'And do not stretch it forth completely' (al-Isra 17:29). And it was said: He would not save anything for tomorrow. And the highest of worldly goods and leadership were offered to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond; rather, he opposed the powerful, the kings, and the chiefs of God until God honored him with fear in the hearts of creation, so that whenever he set out against them in war they feared him. And it was said to him: 'God will protect you from the people' (al-Ma'ida 5:67), so he did not fear them after that, nor is it mentioned that he turned his back to them, despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships, and he promised that the dominion of his community would reach what was folded for him of the earth from east to west, and what has been narrated concerning the types of terror in the hearts of his enemies.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) based on his essential perfection and moral character. The author begins by stating that prophethood is established through three things: the essence (al-jawhar), sensory and intellectual signs, and the agreement of the circumstances of need. He then focuses on the first proof: the essence. This refers to the Prophet's physical and spiritual perfection as inherent in his person. He mentions that the Prophet's face was more beautiful than the full moon, his scent was sweeter than musk, his body softer than silk, and his sweat was used in perfume. His description surpasses any known human perfection. The author argues that freedom from all defects and adornment with every virtue prove that he deserves the highest rank in creation and the best capacities. Additional evidence is that no lie or slip was ever known from him; he never fled from enemies nor had any evil in his character. He was not contentious, never used obscenity, and did not seek revenge for himself. His compassion was so great that God reproached him for excessive grief over his people, quoting verses such as 'So do not let your soul be consumed in regret over them' (35:8) and 'Perhaps you would kill yourself' (26:3). God consoled him with 'Do not grieve over them' (16:127) and praised his mercy in 'Grievous to him is what you suffer' (9:128). His generosity was such that he was instructed not to be extravagant (17:29), and he never saved anything for tomorrow. When offered worldly wealth and leadership in exchange for compromise, he refused and opposed the powerful and the kings. God granted him victory through fear instilled in enemies, and he was assured of divine protection (5:67), so he never feared them. Despite the hardships faced by his followers, he promised that the dominion of his community would extend from east to west. The passage closes by referring to the fear in the hearts of his enemies.

Key Terms
الإشفاق
الكرم
الرعب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that moral character is not sufficient evidence for prophethood.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the perfect and consistent moral character of the Prophet, supported by divine intervention, is a strong proof.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the Prophet reject when offered to him?
A) A kingdom
B) Worldly goods and leadership in exchange for compromising his message
C) A treaty with enemies
D) A marriage proposal

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's flawless character, including his compassion, generosity, and courage, provides compelling evidence of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the Prophet's traits mentioned in this passage do you lack most in your daily interactions, and what one concrete step will you take today to embody it?
?
The Prophet refused worldly leadership to compromise his message. What temptation are you currently facing that could cause you to compromise your faith, and how will you resist it?
?
Are you truly compassionate and generous like the Prophet, or do you hold back for fear of poverty? What would it take for you to trust Allah's provision and give freely?

Introduction to Sensory Miracles: Moon, Tree, and Stone Signs
Maturidi enumerates the first sensory miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first three sensory miracles of the Prophet and how they serve as clear proofs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
God's protection and tangible miracles affirm the Prophet's truthfulness.

Maturidi begins by highlighting God's unwavering protection of the Prophet despite opposition. He then introduces the category of sensory miracles (al-ayat al-hissiyya), starting with three extraordinary events: the splitting of the moon, the tree drawing near, and the stone greeting him. These miracles were witnessed and acknowledged, establishing a foundation for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the Arabic from 'والحفظ عنه' to 'ظهورا' then the translation. Notice Maturidi's emphasis on divine protection.
This sets the context: all plots failed and the Prophet only increased in prominence.
2
Study the three miracles
Identify 'انشقاق القمر', 'اجتذاب الشجر', and 'تسليم الحجر'. Understand each as a literal, witnessed event.
These miracles are sensory – they can be seen and confirmed by the senses.
3
Connect to prophethood
Reflect on how these miracles serve as evidence for the truth of the Prophet's message.
The passage states 'ظاهر ذلك كله عرفوه' – they were apparent and known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحفظ عنه عما راموا به، على موالاة أقربائه الأبعدين في ذلك، وما اجتمعت آراؤهم على إطفاء نوره وطمس أثره، فما ازداد إلا ظهورا. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم الآيات الحسية انشقاق القمر واجتذاب الشجر وتسليم الحجر عليه، ظاهر ذلك كله، عرفوه. ثم شربهم من الماء القليل الكثير من البشر، ثم ابتلاء أعدائه بدعائه بالجدب والقحط ثم استغاثوا به فأغيثوا، ثم الإشباع باليسير من الطعام الكثير من الخلق، ثم أمر بيت المقدس، ثم أمر مرور من طلبوه بالغار فأعمى الله بصرهم، وحنين الخشب، وشكاية الناقة، وشهادة الشاة المصلية؛ ثم ما ساخ بفرس
And [God's] protection of him from what they plotted against him, despite the allegiance of his distant relatives in that, and their opinions united to extinguish his light and erase his trace, but he only increased in prominence. And there is no power except with God. Then the sensory signs: the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, the salutation of the stone to him – all of that is apparent, they recognized it. Then their drinking of much water from little water of the people, then the affliction of his enemies by his prayer with drought and famine, then they sought his help and were helped, then the feeding of many people with little food, then the matter of Jerusalem, then the matter of the passing of those who sought him in the cave and God blinded their sight, and the weeping of the wood, and the complaint of the camel, and the testimony of the roasted sheep; then what sank with a horse.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of sensory miracles (al-ayat al-hissiyya) that the Prophet Muhammad performed, serving as proofs of his prophethood. It begins with a general statement about God's protection of the Prophet despite opposition from his own relatives, and that all plots failed. Then it lists specific miracles: 1) the splitting of the moon, 2) the tree drawing towards him, 3) the stone greeting him, 4) providing abundant water from a small amount, 5) causing drought upon enemies then relieving them, 6) feeding many with little food, 7) the description of Jerusalem after the Night Journey, 8) the protection in the cave by blinding the pursuers, 9) the weeping of the wooden trunk, 10) the complaint of the camel, 11) the testimony of the roasted sheep, and 12) an obscure miracle of something sinking with a horse. Each miracle is presented as witnessed and known, establishing the Prophet's truthfulness.

Key Terms
الآيات الحسية
انشقاق القمر
اجتذاب الشجر
تسليم الحجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These miracles are symbolic or metaphorical events.
Correction: Maturidi presents them as literal sensory occurrences witnessed by people, as indicated by 'ظاهر ذلك كله عرفوه' (all of that is apparent, they recognized it).

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the first three sensory miracles listed by Maturidi?
A) Splitting of the moon
B) Tree drawing near
C) Water flowing from fingers
D) Stone greeting the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The first three sensory miracles (moon, tree, stone) were clear, witnessed events that affirm the Prophet's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The stone greeted the Prophet. If inanimate creation can recognize the truth so readily, what does your hesitation to obey Allah say about your own heart? Will you respond to His signs with the same immediacy as the stone?
?
God's protection kept the Prophet increasing in prominence despite the plots of his distant relatives. Who in your life might be a 'distant relative'—someone close yet opposing your faith? Are you willing to trust God's protection over their approval?
?
The passage says these miracles were 'apparent and recognized.' The greatest miracle you have is the Quran. Is it truly apparent to you, or have you let familiarity make it invisible? What one change will you make today to recognize it as a living sign from Allah?

Sensory Miracles of the Prophet
Enumeration of sensory miracles as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the variety of sensory miracles attributed to the Prophet Muhammad and how they serve as tangible evidence of his prophethood in Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
Sensory miracles were undeniable signs witnessed by contemporaries.

Imam Maturidi presents a list of physical miracles that the Prophet performed, from cosmic events like the splitting of the moon to interactions with animals and objects. These miracles were manifest and recognized by the people of the time. In this lesson, we will go through each miracle and see how they collectively testify to his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage silently, then follow with the English translation. Notice the rhythmic enumeration of miracles.
The phrase 'ظاهر ذلك كله عرفوه' emphasizes that these were evident to observers.
2
Identify each miracle
As you read, make a mental or written list of each miracle mentioned. Pay attention to the variety: cosmic, natural, animal, and providential.
There are at least ten distinct miracles listed.
3
Reflect on their evidential value
Ask yourself: Why would these particular events be persuasive proofs of prophethood? Consider that they were public, witnessed, and beyond normal human capacity.
Maturidi uses them to support the truth of the Prophet's message.

٤ ثم الآيات الحسية مثل انشقاق القمر واجتذاب الشجر وتسليم الحجر عليه، ظاهر ذلك كله عرفوه. ثم شربهم من الماء القليل الكثير من البشر، ثم ابتلاء أعدائه بدعائه بالجدب والقحط ثم استغاثوا به فأغيثوا، ثم الإشباع باليسير من الطعام الكثير من الخلق، ثم أمر بيت المقدس، ثم أمر مرور من طلبوه بالغار فأعمى الله بصرهم، وحنين الخشب، وشكاية الناقة، وشهادة الشاة المصلية؛ ثم ما ساخت [؟] بفرس من اتبعه الأرض.
4. Then the sensory miracles, such as the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, and the greeting of the stone to him; all that was apparent, they recognized it. Then their drinking of much water from a little water for many people; then the affliction of his enemies by his supplication with drought and famine, then they sought relief from him and were relieved; then the feeding of many creation with a little food; then the matter of Jerusalem; then the matter of the passing of those who sought him in the cave and Allah blinded their sight; and the yearning of the wooden trunk, and the complaint of the camel, and the testimony of the roasted sheep; then the sinking of a horse of those who followed him into the ground.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of sensory miracles (الآيات الحسية) performed by the Prophet Muhammad, presented as evidence of his prophethood. The author lists them in sequence: the splitting of the moon, the drawing of a tree towards him, the greeting of a stone, the multiplication of water for many people from a small amount, the relief from drought through his supplication, the feeding of many with little food, his description of Jerusalem, the blinding of the pursuers in the cave, the yearning of the wooden trunk (the pulpit), the complaint of a camel, the testimony of a roasted sheep, and the sinking of a horse belonging to a follower into the ground. Each miracle is presented as a clear sign that the people recognized. The phrase 'ظاهر ذلك كله عرفوه' (all that was apparent, they recognized it) indicates that these miracles were undeniable to those who witnessed them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These miracles are merely legendary stories without historical basis.
Correction: The passage asserts that these miracles were evident and recognized by contemporaries, implying they were witnessed and accepted as real events.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'الآيات الحسية' in this passage?
A) Rational proofs
B) Sensory miracles
C) Legal rulings

Key Takeaway
The sensory miracles are tangible proofs of prophethood that were clearly witnessed by contemporaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about ten clear, undeniable miracles that the Prophet's contemporaries witnessed. If you had been one of them, would you have believed immediately? What is holding you back from having that same certainty today? This week, identify one moment where you acted as if these miracles are 'just stories' and repent from that attitude.
?
The passage says these miracles were 'apparent' and 'recognized' by the people. Yet many still disbelieved. In your own journey of faith, what 'clear signs' has Allah shown you that you have brushed aside? Will you today make a firm intention to respond to Allah's signs with immediate obedience, no matter how small?
?
Consider the camel that complained to the Prophet about its hardship. The Prophet listened. When your own soul or body complains to you through fatigue or anxiety, do you dismiss it or do you pause and turn to Allah? Write down one practical step you will take this week to treat yourself like the Prophet treated that camel—with mercy and attention.

Prophecies as Proof of Prophethood
Enumeration of prophecies as evidence of prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fulfillment of specific prophecies made by the Prophet Muhammad serves as compelling evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies are tangible signs of divine knowledge and truthfulness.

Prophecies are a form of miracle (kharq al-‘ādah) that demonstrate the Prophet's connection to divine revelation. In this passage, Imam al-Māturīdī lists several prophecies from the Quran and hadith that were precisely fulfilled. As you read, consider how each prediction could not have been made from human knowledge alone, affirming that the Prophet spoke from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the pattern: each prophecy begins with a statement ('he informed') followed by its fulfillment.
The passage uses the term 'إخبار' (informing) repeatedly.
2
Identify each prophecy
The passage lists several distinct prophecies. Go through them one by one: the Jews' desire for death, polytheists' inability to plot, hypocrisy exposed, prophecies about Abu Bakr and apostasy, Ali killing the breakers of covenant, and Ammar's death.
Each prophecy is connected to a Quranic verse or authentic hadith.
3
Reflect on the proof
Ask yourself: Could any human have known these specific outcomes beforehand? The very specificity and fulfillment show that the Prophet's knowledge came from Allah, confirming his prophethood.
This is the core argument: accurate future knowledge is a sign of prophecy.
4
Test your understanding
After studying the commentary, take the checkpoint quiz to see if you can recall which prophecies were mentioned and what they proved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ما أخبر من قوله: ولا يتمنونه وكان كذلك، ثم بما قال: (وادعوا شركاءكم ثم كيدون فلا تنظرون) ما قدروا عليه، ثم بكثرة ما يمكرونه حتى خلصه الله من ذلك، وبعظيم ما يضمر أهل النفاق في أنفسهم، فأطلعه حتى كانوا مع شدة تعنتهم يحذرون نزول سورة تنبتهم بما كان قالوا فيه وفي متبعيه. وما قال في أبي بكر وأصحابه من قوله: (أفإن مات أو قتل انقلبتم على أعقابكم) الآية، وكذلك في قوله: (ومن يرتد منكم عن دينه) الآية، وما أظهره الله منهم على ما أعلم عليا أنه يقتل الناكثين المارقين، وكان كذلك، وما قال لعمار: (تقتلك الفئة الباغية).
Then what he informed of his statement: 'They will never desire it' and it was so; then by his saying: 'Call your partners then plot against me and give me no respite' - they were not able to do it; then by the abundance of their plotting until Allah delivered him from that; and by the great hypocrisy that the people of hypocrisy concealed, so He informed him of it until despite their intense stubbornness they feared the revelation of a surah that would expose what they said about him and his followers. And what he said about Abu Bakr and his companions from his statement: 'If he dies or is killed, will you turn back on your heels?' and likewise in his statement: 'Whoever among you apostatizes from his religion...' and what Allah manifested from them on what He informed Ali that he would kill the breakers of covenant and the renegades, and it was so; and what he said to Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you.'
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents a series of prophecies (إخبار) made by the Prophet Muhammad that were fulfilled exactly as he foretold, serving as further evidence of his prophethood. The author lists: the prophecy that the Jews would not desire death (referring to Quran 62:6-7), the challenge to the polytheists to call their partners and plot against him (Quran 7:195) which they failed to do, the foiling of their plots, the exposure of the hypocrites' inner thoughts such that they feared revelation of a surah exposing them, the prophecies about Abu Bakr and the companions regarding apostasy (Quran 3:144 and 5:54), the prophecy about Ali killing the breakers of covenant (الناكثين) and the renegades (المارقين) which came true, and the prophecy to Ammar that the rebellious group (الفئة الباغية) would kill him. The fulfillment of these prophecies confirms the truth of his message.

Key Terms

الناكثين
المارقين
الفئة الباغية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these prophecies were coincidences or vague predictions that could have had multiple interpretations.
Correction: The prophecies are highly specific and were literally fulfilled, which cannot be explained by coincidence. They demonstrate knowledge beyond human capability, affirming the Prophet's truthfulness.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The specific fulfillment of prophecies made by the Prophet serves as a clear sign that his knowledge came from Allah, confirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one promise you struggle to fully trust, and what step can you take today to strengthen that trust?
?
When you read about the hypocrites whose inner thoughts were exposed, does it make you examine your own sincerity? Ask yourself: if all my hidden thoughts were revealed tomorrow, would I be ashamed? What one hidden motive do you need to repent from right now?
?
The prophecy about Ammar being killed by the rebellious group came true despite all efforts. Are you willing to accept that Allah's decree will always prevail, even when your own plans fail? What is one area of your life where you are resisting submission to His plan, and how will you surrender it today?

Sensory Proofs of Prophethood from Fulfilled Prophecies
Maturidi enumerates sensory miracles and prophecies that prove prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses fulfilled prophecies as sensory evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies are tangible proof that the Prophet spoke with divine knowledge.

In this passage from Kitab al-Tawhid, Imam al-Maturidi presents a series of concrete predictions made by the Prophet Muhammad that came true exactly as foretold. These include challenges to his opponents, revelations about hidden intentions, and specific events involving his companions. These prophecies, witnessed by both believers and enemies, serve as sensory proofs of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the examples enumerated.
Notice the variety of examples: from Quranic challenges to prophetic announcements.
2
Identify categories of prophecies
Group the examples into categories: prophecies about enemies (Jews, polytheists), about hypocrites, about companions (Abu Bakr, Ali, Ammar), and about future conquests.
This helps see the breadth of evidence.
3
Understand the argument for objectivity
Maturidi notes that these events were apparent even to enemies. Ask yourself why this strengthens the proof.
Sensory evidence means it was witnessed or known publicly.
4
Reflect on the cumulative weight
Consider how multiple fulfilled prophecies, impossible to be human guesses, collectively confirm prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من اتبعه الأرض . ثم ما أخبر من قوله : ولا يتمنونه وكان كذلك، ثم بما قال: وادعوا شركاءكم ثم كيدون فلا تنظرون ما قدروا عليه، ثم بكثرة ما يمكرونه حتى خلصه الله من ذلك، وبعظيم ما يضمر أهل النفاق في أنفسهم، فأطلعه حتى كانوا مع شدة تعنتهم يحذرون نزول سورة تنبتهم بما كان قالوا فيه وفي متبعيه. وما قال في أبي بكر وأصحابه من قوله : أفإن مات أو قتل انقلبتم على أعقابكم، الآية، وكذلك في قوله : ومن يرتد منكم عن دينه الآية، وأظهره على ما أعلم عليا أنه يقتل الناكثين المارقين، وكان كذلك، وما قال لعمار: «تقتلك الفئة الباغية، وما وعد من الفتوح وسعة الدنيا على المؤمنين، وغير ذلك مما يكثر ذكره لو استقصى فيه، رواه نجباء أمته. ثم عامة ذلك مما كان ظاهرا عند أعدائه. مع ما كان في الكتب المنزلة بعثه، وعلى ألسن الرسل جرت البشارة وأخذ العهد عليه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Those who followed him on earth. Then what He informed of His saying: 'And they do not wish for it' and it was so, then by what He said: 'Call your partners then plot against me and give me no respite' they could not do it, then by the abundance of their plotting until Allah delivered him from that, and by the great things that the hypocrites concealed in themselves, so He informed him until they, despite their severe obstinacy, feared the revelation of a surah that would inform them of what they had said concerning him and his followers. And what He said concerning Abu Bakr and his companions in His saying: 'Then if he dies or is killed, will you turn back on your heels?' the verse, and likewise in His saying: 'And whoever among you turns back from his religion' the verse, and He made manifest what He had informed Ali that he would kill the covenant-breakers, the renegades, and it was so, and what He said to Ammar: 'You will be killed by the transgressing faction', and what He promised of conquests and expansion of the world for the believers, and other things that would be too many to mention if one sought to exhaust them, related by the nobles of his community. Then all of that was apparent to his enemies. Along with what was in the revealed books concerning his sending, and on the tongues of the messengers the good tidings were given and the covenant was taken for him. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage enumerates sensory proofs of prophethood, specifically fulfilled prophecies and miraculous events. The author lists several examples: the Jews' inability to wish for death as challenged in the Quran; the failure of the polytheists' plots despite their efforts; the Prophet's knowledge of the hypocrites' secrets; the prophecies about Abu Bakr and the companions; the prediction about Ali killing the covenant-breakers (the people of the Camel) and the renegades (the Khawarij); the prophecy to Ammar that he would be killed by the transgressing faction; and promises of future conquests. These were all narrated by trustworthy members of the community and were evident even to enemies. Moreover, previous scriptures had foretold his coming, and covenants were taken from earlier prophets concerning him. The passage concludes with a phrase recognizing divine power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: Maturidi states that 'all of that was apparent to his enemies', highlighting that fulfilled prophecies are objective evidence, not merely subjective belief.

The Quran as a Rational Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi enumerates the Quran's rational proofs: inimitability, arguments for tawhid and resurrection, and foreknowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's inimitability and unique content serve as a rational proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's unmatched speech and knowledge prove it is from Allah.

Maturidi begins his rational proofs by directing attention to the Quran itself. He argues that its linguistic perfection, its unprecedented arguments for divine unity and resurrection, and its accurate prophecies of future events are beyond human capacity. These features, accessible to reason, establish the truth of the Prophet's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Quran's rational proof
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi structures the proof around three aspects of the Quran.
2
Identify the three aspects highlighted
List the three specific features Maturidi mentions: linguistic inimitability, arguments for tawhid and resurrection, and prophecies of future events.
These are rational proofs because they can be recognized by human intellects, not just through transmission.
3
Reflect on why these are rational proofs
Consider how each aspect exceeds human capacity, making the Quran's divine origin and the Prophet's truth evident to reason.
Think about why Maturidi might consider these rational rather than sensory proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جـ) وأما العقلية فما بيّن الله من شأن القرآن الذي إنما يعرف خروجه عن احتمال وسع الخلق من بالغ في فنون الآداب وعرف جواهر الكلام وأصنافه؛ ثم ما فيه من المحاجة في توحيد الرب وأدلة البعث مما لم يكن يومئذ على وجه الأرض من يدعى ذلك؛ ثم ما فيه من الأنباء وما يكون أبدا، ومن بيان النوازل التي تكون مما [ليس] في استعمال العقول تطلع عليه. وذكر أبو زيد أن الحسية من الآيات فما جاءت من الآثار الكافية. وأما العقلية فهي على وجوه أحدها أن أمره لم يكن مستغربًا، بل كان مستمرا على العادة بوجود مثله في الأمم، فلذلك يبطل وجه الرد عليه في أول وهلة. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وإن من أمة إلا خلا فيها نذير﴾ [فاطر، ٢٤/٣٥]، وقال : ولكل قوم هاد، وقال: ثم أرسلنا رسلنا
C) As for the rational proofs, they are what Allah has shown concerning the Quran, which is known to exceed the capacity of creatures—to one proficient in the arts of literature and acquainted with the gems of speech and its varieties. Then what is in it of argumentation concerning the tawhid of the Lord and proofs of the resurrection, which at that time there was no one on the face of the earth claiming that. Then what is in it of news of what will be forever, and the explanation of calamities that occur, which [not] within the use of intellects to attain. And Abu Zaid mentioned that the sensory proofs among the signs are what came from sufficient reports. And as for the rational proofs, they are in several aspects: one of them is that his affair was not strange, but was continuous according to custom with the existence of the like among nations, so the ground for rejection is nullified at first glance. Allah the Exalted said: 'And there was no nation but that a warner had passed among them' [Fatir 35:24], and He said: 'And for every people there is a guide', and He said: 'Then We sent Our messengers'.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents rational proofs of prophethood. First, the Quran itself is a rational proof: its inimitability is recognized by experts in literature and speech; it contains arguments for tawhid and resurrection that were unprecedented; it includes prophecies and explanations of events beyond human intellect. Then the author mentions Abu Zaid's view that sensory proofs come from sufficient reports. Finally, the second rational proof: the Prophet's mission was not unprecedented; rather, similar messengers were sent to every nation, so rejecting him outright is invalid. This is supported by Quranic verses stating that every nation had a warner and a guide, and that Allah sent messengers.

Key Terms
الآيات العقلية
الإعجاز
توحيد الرب
أدلة البعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational proofs of prophethood are only found in philosophical arguments, not in the Quran itself.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the Quran's own content—its inimitability, arguments, and prophecies—constitute rational proofs accessible to reason.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the first rational proof of prophethood?
A) The miracle of the splitting of the moon
B) The Quran's inimitability and its content
C) The testimony of previous scriptures
D) The Prophet's character

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself provides rational proof of prophethood through its unmatched linguistic quality, unprecedented arguments, and knowledge of the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you actively engage with its rational arguments, or do you passively accept its authority? How would your faith change if you truly grasped these proofs?
?
The Quran contains knowledge of future calamities and events that human intellect cannot reach. In moments of uncertainty in your life, do you turn to the Quran for guidance, trusting that its knowledge is from Allah?
?
Maturidi emphasizes that the Quran's arguments for tawhid were unprecedented. Do you take these arguments for granted, or do you ponder them as if hearing them for the first time? What would it mean to live with a fresh awareness of the Quran's unique proof?

The Continuity of Prophethood as a Rational Proof
Maturidi argues that the continuous sending of prophets validates Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consistent pattern of sending prophets to all nations serves as a rational proof for Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a continuous, universal tradition, not an anomaly.

Maturidi presents a second rational proof: the mission of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is not a strange, unprecedented event. Rather, Allah sent warners to every previous nation. This historical consistency makes rejection unreasonable. The lesson explores this argument and its Quranic foundations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the second rational proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the transition from Abu Zaid's classification to Maturidi's argument about continuity.
2
Understand the logical structure
The argument: prophets were sent to all nations, so the claim of a new prophet is not novel. Therefore, rejection based on strangeness is invalid.
This is a rational proof based on historical pattern, not on a specific miracle.
3
Examine the Quranic verses cited
Look at the three citations: 'And there was no nation but that a warner had passed among them', 'And for every people there is a guide', and 'Then We sent Our messengers'. How do they support the argument?
The verses establish the universality of prophethood.
4
Compare with the first proof
This proof complements the Quranic proof by addressing initial skepticism based on novelty, while the first proof provides positive evidence from the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah has sent a warner to every nation, including yours, what is your excuse for not following the message of Muhammad? Are you truly convinced you have no accountability?
?
The Prophet's mission was not strange—it fit a divine pattern. But does your life reflect that pattern of submission? Where are you still treating your own path as an exception to Allah's guidance?
?
Maturidi says rejection is nullified 'at first glance.' When you hear the call of Islam, do you reject it because it seems unfamiliar? Or do you recognize it as part of the truth that has come to every people? What stops you from accepting it fully?
