The Quran as a Rational Sign of Prophethood
Maturidi defines rational signs through the Quran's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran itself serves as a rational proof of prophethood through its miraculous eloquence, its unique arguments for tawhid and resurrection, and its predictions of future events.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability is a rational sign that demands intellectual engagement.

In this passage, Maturidi first defines rational signs of prophethood by pointing to the Quran. Unlike sensory signs based on reports, the Quran's miraculous nature is accessible to reason. He highlights three aspects: its literary excellence beyond human capacity, its unprecedented arguments for divine unity and resurrection, and its accurate news of past and future. This lesson explores these dimensions, establishing the Quran as an enduring rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Quran's qualities
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi describes three distinct aspects of the Quran as a rational sign.
2
Identify the three aspects
The passage lists three 'then' (ثم) clauses. Identify each: literary inimitability, theological arguments, and news of unseen events.
Each aspect is a separate proof.
3
Reflect on the requirement of expertise
Maturidi says the Quran's miraculous nature is known only by one who has mastered the arts of literature. Consider why this makes it a rational rather than sensory sign.
Rational signs require intellectual effort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج) وأما العقلية فما بيّن الله من شأن القرآن الذي إنما يعرف خروجه عن احتمال وسع الخلق من بالغ في فنون الآداب وعرف جواهر الكلام وأصنافه ؛ ثم ما فيه من المحاجة في توحيد الرب وأدلة البعث مما لم يكن يومئذ على وجه الأرض من يدعى ذلك؛ ثم ما فيه من الأنباء وما يكون أبدا، ومن بيان النوازل التي تكون مما [ليس] في استعمال العقول تطلع عليه. وذكر أبو زيد أن الحسية من الآيات فما جاءت من الآثار الكافية. وأما العقلية فهي على وجوه أحدها أن أمره لم يكن مستغربًا، بل كان مستمرا على العادة بوجود مثله في الأمم، فلذلك يبطل وجه الرد عليه في أول وهلة . قال الله تعالى: ﴿وإن من أمة إلا خلا فيها نذير﴾ [فاطر، ٢٤/٣٥]، وقال : ولكل قوم هاد، وقال: ثم أرسلنا رسلنا تترى ﴾ [المؤمنون، ٤٤/٢٣] . والثاني موافقة مجيئه وقت الحاجة إليه، إذ كان زمان فترة ودرس العلم، مع جزي عادة الله بمعاقبة أسباب الهداية عند زوال أهله عن نهج الهدى. قال الله تعالى: قد جاءكم رسولنا يبين لكم " ، الآية " . والثالث كون المبعوث فيهم بموضع الحاجة إليه الخلاء جنسه عن أسباب العلم بقوله : هو الذي بعث في الأميين رسولاً منهم ، وغيره. والرابع كونه في أظهر الأماكن للخلق، إذ هو معالم أهل الآفاق في الدنيا، وقال الله تعالى: وكذلك أوحينا إليك ، الآية" . والخامس تمنى القوم ذلك وإظهار الرغبة في ذلك، وإذا اقترح مقترح على ربه إزالة علته لم يكن تعجب قطع معذرته، قال الله تعالى: ولو أنا أهلكناهم بعذاب من قبله ، الآية " ، قال : وأقسموا بالله جهد أيمانهم لئن جاءهم نذير " ، الآية " . فهذه الخمسة مما حاجهم به في أحوالهم
C) As for the rational (signs), they are what God has made clear concerning the matter of the Quran, whose surpassing of the capacity of creation is known only by one who has mastered the arts of literature and knows the jewels of speech and its kinds; then what it contains of argument about the Oneness of the Lord and the proofs of the resurrection, which at that time there was no one on the face of the earth who claimed that; then what it contains of news and what will be forever, and of the explanation of events that occur, which [is not] within the use of intellects to attain. And Abu Zaid mentioned that the sensory (signs) from the signs are those that came from sufficient reports. As for the rational (signs), they are in modes: The first is that his affair was not strange, but rather continuous according to custom by the existence of his like among the nations, and due to that the aspect of rejection of him is nullified at first glance. God Almighty said: “And there is no nation but there has passed away in it a warner” [Fatir, 24/35], and He said: “And for every people there is a guide”, and He said: “Then We sent Our messengers in succession” [Al-Mu'minun, 23/44]. The second is the concurrence of his coming at the time of need for him, because it was a time of interval and effacement of knowledge, along with the portion of God's custom of punishing the causes of guidance when its people deviate from the path of guidance. God Almighty said: “Indeed, Our messenger has come to you, making clear to you”, the verse. The third is that the one sent among them was in a position of need for him, his type being devoid of means of knowledge by His saying: “It is He who has sent among the unlettered a messenger from among them”, and others. The fourth is that he was in the most prominent places for creation, for he is a landmark for the people of the horizons in the world, and God Almighty said: “And thus We have revealed to you”, the verse. The fifth is the people's wish for that and their showing desire for it, and if a proposer proposes to his Lord the removal of his excuse, it is not surprising that his excuse is cut off. God Almighty said: “And if We had destroyed them with a punishment before it”, the verse, and He said: “And they swore by God with their strongest oaths that if a warner came to them”, the verse. These are the five by which he argued against them in their conditions.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies the rational signs (العقلية) of prophethood as distinct from sensory signs (الحسية). The author first notes that the Quran itself is a rational sign because its miraculous nature is recognized by those learned in eloquence, and it contains arguments for tawhid and resurrection. Then he reports Abu Zaid's view that sensory signs come from reliable reports, while rational signs are of several modes. He then enumerates five modes: (1) The prophet's coming was not unprecedented; similar messengers had been sent to every nation, so it was consistent with God's custom. (2) His coming coincided with a time of need—a period between messengers when knowledge had faded—so it fulfilled the divine pattern of sending guidance when people stray. (3) The messenger was sent from among the unlettered (أميين), so he could not have acquired his knowledge from human sources. (4) He was sent from the most prominent location (Mecca), which is a landmark for people, making his mission widely accessible. (5) The people themselves had wished for a messenger and sworn that if one came they would follow; thus their rejection after his coming would leave them without excuse. Each mode is supported by a Quranic verse. The passage concludes that these five arguments were used against the deniers of his prophethood. The author here faithfully reports Abu Zaid's classification as part of a broader discussion of proofs.

Key Terms
عقلية
قرآن
إعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational signs are merely abstract philosophical proofs unrelated to scripture.
Correction: This passage shows rational signs are grounded in the concrete attributes of the Quran—its literary excellence, arguments, and prophetic news.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is NOT mentioned as a quality of the Quran that makes it a rational sign?
A) Its literary inimitability
B) Its arguments for tawhid and resurrection
C) Its detailed legal rulings
D) Its news of past and future

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself is a rational sign of prophethood because its literary, theological, and predictive dimensions exceed human capability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you actively engage with its arguments for tawhid and the resurrection, or do you take them for granted? Today, commit to reflecting on one specific Quranic proof for God's oneness and write down how it strengthens your conviction.
?
The Quran's rational signs demand intellectual effort from you. Have you ever studied its literary inimitability or teachings about the unseen with the seriousness they deserve? Will you set aside time this week to learn about the Quran's miraculous aspects?
?
If the Quran is indeed a rational proof of prophethood, why do you still sometimes doubt or feel uncertain? Ask yourself: Am I treating the Quran as a mere recitation or as a living argument that calls me to respond? What one step will you take today to make the Quran's rational signs central to your faith?

Abu Zaid's Five Rational Signs of Prophethood
Abu Zaid enumerates five rational modes of prophethood with Quranic support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five rational signs of prophethood as enumerated by Abu Zaid, each grounded in divine custom and Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Rational signs of prophethood are found in the patterns of divine custom and human need.

After presenting the Quran as a prime rational sign, Maturidi reports Abu Zaid's classification of sensory and rational signs. Sensory signs come from reliable reports, but rational signs are reasoned deductions. Abu Zaid then lists five modes: the prophet's coming was not unprecedented, it was timely, he was sent from among the unlettered, from the most prominent place, and the people had wished for him. Each is supported by Quranic verses. This lesson examines these five arguments, showing how they refute denial at its root.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sensory and rational signs
Read the two lines defining sensory and rational signs. Notice that sensory signs come from reports, while rational signs are based on reasoning.
Abu Zaid's classification is a key framework.
2
List the five rational modes
The passage enumerates five modes (وجوه) with the words 'أحدها', 'والثاني', etc. Identify each one.
Each mode is a distinct argument.
3
Match each mode to its Quranic verse
For each mode, the author cites a supporting verse. Write down the verse reference or part of the verse.
The verses are cut short with 'الآية'.
4
Consider the cumulative force
Reflect on how these five arguments together leave no room for valid rejection of the prophet.
The passage says they argue against deniers 'في أحوالهم'.

The Prophet's Unlettered Background as Proof
Maturidi begins listing arguments from the Prophet's personal background.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's upbringing among an unlettered people and his own lack of formal study support the divine origin of his message.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unlettered background shows his knowledge came from Allah, not human learning.

Maturidi continues his defense of prophethood by turning to the personal circumstances of the Prophet Muhammad. He argues that the Prophet's environment and his own lack of education rule out human acquisition of the knowledge he brought. This passage begins a new line of reasoning that complements the earlier arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two parts: the condition of the Prophet's people and his own lack of prior study.
The passage is incomplete but forms a natural unit for this argument.
2
Identify the key points
The passage gives three interconnected facts: (1) his people had no books or study, (2) he did not leave them to learn elsewhere, (3) they had no books for him to practice study.
3
Understand the logic
Ask yourself: why do these facts support prophethood? The answer is that the Prophet's knowledge could not have come from human sources, so it must be from divine revelation.
This is a classic argument for the miraculous nature of the Quran.
4
Consider the misconception
Some might think this denies any human teachers, but the argument specifically targets book learning and formal study. The Prophet learned from Allah directly.
The Prophet did have human interactions, but his core message was revealed.

Commentary
This passage introduces a second set of arguments for prophethood focusing on the personal background of the Prophet Muhammad. The author argues that the Prophet grew up in a community that lacked scriptures and formal education ('لم يكن لهم كتب ولا دراسة'), and he himself did not leave his people to acquire knowledge elsewhere. Moreover, there were no books in which he could have trained himself in study before his mission. This highlights that the knowledge he brought could not have been acquired through human means, pointing to divine revelation. The argument is incomplete in this window, but the rationale is clear: the Prophet's humble, unlettered background supports the claim that his message came from God. The commentary follows the author's own order: first the condition of his people (no books, no study) and then his own lack of prior training.

Four Rational Arguments for Prophethood from Human Conditions
Maturidi enumerates four arguments (Second through Fifth) from the people's conditions for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four distinct arguments that Imam Maturidi derives from the conditions of the people to prove the necessity of sending prophets.

Core Idea
Human need and desire itself demands divine guidance.

Imam Maturidi presents a series of compelling arguments rooted in the state of humanity itself. Rather than starting from abstract theology, he looks at the actual situation of people—their need for guidance, their ignorance, their location, and even their own wishes—to show why prophets are not only plausible but necessary. This passage lays out four such arguments, each supported by a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Notice how each argument is introduced with 'The second...', 'The third...', etc.
These arguments follow a missing first argument; we see only the last four.
2
Identify each argument and its Quranic proof
For each of the four arguments, note the key point Maturidi makes and the verse he cites. Try to understand how each argument arises from the people's condition.
3
Reflect on the logical connection
Ask yourself: How does each argument show that sending a prophet is not just possible but necessary? What would be missing if no prophet came?
4
Summarize the collective force of the arguments
Consider how these four arguments together build a case that prophethood is a rational requirement given human circumstances.
Maturidi uses both reason and revelation (Quran) to prove his point.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The second: the correspondence of his coming to the time of need for him, since it was a time of interval and the disappearance of knowledge, along with the continuation of God’s custom of punishing the means of guidance when its people depart from the path of guidance. Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage enumerates five arguments (second through fifth, the first being absent) that Maturidi uses to argue for the necessity of prophethood from the conditions of the people themselves. The second argument is that the messenger came at a time of need, when there was a period of interval between prophets and knowledge had vanished, and God's custom is to provide guidance when people deviate. The third argument is that the messenger was sent to a people who were devoid of means of knowledge, as they were unlettered. The fourth is that he was sent in the most apparent place, serving as a guide for people far and wide. The fifth is that the people themselves longed for a warner and swore oaths that they would believe if one came, so God sent him to remove their excuses. Each argument is supported by a Quranic verse.

Key Terms
موافقة مجيئه وقت الحاجة
زمان فترة ودرس العلم
أظهر الأماكن للخلق
تمنى القوم ذلك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second argument Maturidi presents from the conditions of the people?
A) The messenger was sent in the most apparent place.
B) The messenger came at a time of need when knowledge was absent.
C) The people longed for a messenger and swore oaths.
D) The messenger was sent to a people devoid of means of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The conditions of the people themselves—their need, ignorance, location, and desires—provide rational grounds for the necessity of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were living in a time without a prophet, would you truly seek one? Or would you rely solely on your own intellect? What does your answer say about your reliance on God's guidance?
?
The third argument highlights that the people were unlettered and lacked knowledge. In what areas of your faith are you still 'unlettered'? What concrete step will you take this week to learn from the prophetic guidance you have?
?
The people swore oaths that if a warner came, they would believe. When you hear the Quran being recited, do you respond with the same urgency? Or do you delay acting? Write a specific commitment you will make today.

Arguments from the Prophet's Personal Conditions
Maturidi argues for prophethood from the prophet's upbringing, unletteredness, and miraculous knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Prophet's personal circumstances—his unletteredness, upbringing, and miraculous knowledge—to prove the divine origin of the Quran and his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unlettered upbringing and lack of training prove the Quran could only be from God.

Maturidi presents a series of arguments from the personal conditions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) to demonstrate that the Quran is divine revelation. He examines the Prophet's social context, his unletteredness, and his inability to produce such eloquent speech through human means. This lesson unpacks these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage uses several Quranic verses as evidence, indicated by 'الآية'.
2
Identify the three main arguments
The passage presents three distinct proofs: (1) the Prophet's upbringing among a people without books, (2) his unletteredness and miraculous memorization, and (3) his lack of training in composing speech. Find each one.
Look for connecting words like 'منها', 'ثم', and 'وأيضاً'.
3
Notice the Quranic citations
Maturidi cites several verses to support his arguments. Reflect on how each verse reinforces the point about the Prophet's conditions.
The verses are abbreviated with 'الآية'; consider looking them up for full context.
4
Reflect on the challenge to produce a surah
The passage ends with the challenge to the disbelievers to produce a surah like the Quran. Their silence is presented as proof of the Quran's divine origin. Ask yourself: why does this silence count as evidence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ما حاجهم بما في أحوال النبي؛ منها أنه نشأ في قوم لم يكن لهم كتب ولا دراسة مع ما لم يفارق قومه، ولا كان لهم كتب قد سبق له الارتياض في دراستها. ثم كان في ضمن ام ودروس. تلك: لو طرأ عليهم طارئ لا يجهل مكانه؛ وذلك قوله: أم لم يعرفوا رسولهم، الآية، وقوله: وتلك من أنباء الغيب نوحيها، الآية. وقد نشأ أميا، والأمي لا يأخذ عن الكتب ولا يستطيع التحفظ من الأفواه غاية الحفظ، إنما يكون ضبطه بصور معقولة روحانية يرتفع به عن الوهم دليله ما لا يوجد عن مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظه القرآن، وقال الله تعالى: سنقرؤك فلا تنسى، الآية، وقال: ولا تحرك به لسانك، الآية؛ ولذلك قيل للموصوف بالحفظ: إنه لأشد تعصبا من قلوب الرجال من النَّعَم من عُقُلها. قال الله تعالى: وما كنت تتلو من قبل من كتاب، الآية. وأيضاً إنه لم يذكر عنه في سالف عمره التشاغل بنظم الكلام والتعاطى من ضروبه. ثم ممتنع عن مثله أن يتهيأ له ما يعجز عنه المعروفون بارتياضه. دليله أنه لم يُطعن بشيء من ذلك، بل لما قيل بقوله قال لهم فأتوا بسورة من مثله، فسكتوا ولم.
Then what he argued with them regarding the conditions of the Prophet: among them is that he grew up among a people who had no books and no study, while he did not leave his people, nor did they have books in which he had previously exercised. Then he was among umm and durus. That: if a sudden arrival came upon them, they would not be ignorant of his place; and that is His saying: 'Or did they not know their Messenger?' – the verse, and His saying: 'And these are from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you' – the verse. And he grew up unlettered, and the unlettered does not take from books and cannot memorize from mouths to the utmost degree of memorization; rather his retention is by spiritual rational images by which he is raised above illusion, the proof of which is that nothing like him is found in the transmission of poems for fear of error and other things. Therefore their amazement at his memorization of the Quran was intense, and God Almighty said: 'We will make you recite, so you will not forget' – the verse, and He said: 'And do not move your tongue with it to hasten it' – the verse; therefore it was said of the one described with memorization: indeed he is more firmly bound than the hearts of men from livestock by their ropes. God Almighty said: 'And you did not recite before it any book' – the verse. And also, it is not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech and engaging in its genres. Then it is impossible for someone like him to prepare what those known for their practice are incapable of. Its proof is that he was not criticized for any of that, but rather when it was said to him, he said to them: 'Then bring a surah like it,' so they were silent and did not.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents arguments for prophethood drawn from the personal conditions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). First, he grew up among a people without scripture or learning, and he did not leave them, so he could not have acquired knowledge externally. Second, if a foreign teacher had come, his influence would have been known, but it was not. Third, he was unlettered; an unlettered person cannot learn from books or memorize perfectly from oral transmission. His retention of the Quran was miraculous, relying on spiritual images beyond illusion. This caused the people to marvel. God promised him preservation from forgetfulness. Fourth, he had no prior training in composing speech or rhetoric, yet produced the Quran which challenged the experts. The proof is that when challenged to produce a similar surah, the opponents were silent and failed.

Key Terms
نشأ أميا
التحفظ من الأفواه
صور معقولة روحانية
نظم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's unletteredness means he was ignorant or illiterate in a way that prevented him from understanding anything.
Correction: Unletteredness (ummi) here refers to not having studied books or been taught by human teachers. It does not imply ignorance; rather, it highlights that the knowledge he brought (the Quran) came directly from God.

Checkpoint
What evidence does Maturidi give to show that the Prophet did not learn the Quran from human sources?
A) The Prophet traveled extensively and studied with scholars.
B) The Prophet grew up among a people without books and was unlettered.
C) The Prophet memorized poetry from oral tradition.
D) The Prophet had teachers who taught him rhetoric.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's personal conditions—his upbringing, unletteredness, and lack of rhetorical training—collectively prove that the Quran is divine revelation, not human composition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's lack of human training is what proves the Quran is from God, then where do you place your trust when you seek truth—in your own expertise and study, or in the possibility that God might speak directly to you through His revelation? Are you willing to admit that your intellect alone cannot reach certainty without divine guidance?
?
The Prophet's unletteredness was not a deficiency but a sign. What is the 'weakness' in your life that you have been ashamed of? Could it be that God has chosen to manifest His power through that very weakness, if only you would submit it to Him? Will you continue to hide it, or will you offer it as a vessel for His strength?
?
The disbelievers had every apparent reason to reject the Prophet, yet his personal conditions and the Quran's inimitability left them silent. When you face evidence for the truth that challenges your convenience or desires, does your heart produce silence—or do you manufacture excuses to avoid submission? What silence are you holding back today?

The Prophet's Illiteracy and Lack of Training
Maturidi presents the argument from the Prophet's known character and illiteracy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Prophet's well-known character and illiteracy as evidence that he could not have authored the Quran.

Core Idea
The Prophet's known illiteracy proves the Quran could not be his own composition.

Maturidi begins by reminding us that the Quraysh knew the Prophet intimately – he was a known enemy of falsehood. Then he highlights his illiteracy: he did not learn from books, had no special memory, and never engaged in composing speech. This passage shows that the Quran's preservation and eloquence were divinely granted, not humanly acquired.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi piles up evidence of the Prophet's lack of training.
Pay attention to the verses quoted.
2
Identify the key arguments
List the specific points: the Quraysh's knowledge of him, his illiteracy, his inability to memorize perfectly, and the divine guarantee of preservation.
These form a cumulative case.
3
Connect to the Quranic verses
See how each verse supports a point: e.g., 'Did they not recognize their Messenger?' refers to his character; 'We will make you recite so you shall not forget' shows divine preservation.
Maturidi is drawing on Quranic evidence.
4
Contrast with the common assumption
Consider that someone without training cannot produce such a masterpiece. The passage refutes the idea that the Prophet could have composed the Quran.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلك : لو طرأ عليهم طارئ لا يجهل مكانه ؛ وذلك قوله : أم لم يعرفوا رسولهم ، وقوله : وتلك من أنباء الغيب نوحيها . وقد نشأ أميا، والأمي لا يأخذ عن الكتب ولا يستطيع التحفظ من الأفواه غاية الحفظ، إنما يكون ضبطه بصور معقولة روحانية يرتفع به عن الوهم دليله ما لا يوجد عن مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظه القرآن، وقال الله تعالى: سنقرؤك فلا تنسى ، وقال : ولا تحرك به لسانك ؛ ولذلك قيل للموصوف بالحفظ : إنه لأشد تعصبا من قلوب الرجال من النعم من عقلها . قال الله تعالى: ﴿وما كنت تتلو من قبله من كتاب . وأيضاً إنه لم يذكر عنه في سالف عمره التشاغل بنظم الكلام والتعاطي من ضروبه . ثم ممتنع عن مثله أن يتهيأ له ما يعجز عنه المعروفون بارتياضه. دليله أنه لم يطعن بشيء من ذلك ، بل لما قيل بقوله قال لهم فأتوا بسورة من مثله ﴾، فسكتوا ولم يدعوا عليه إظهاره فيه. ويعني ذلك أنه لو كان قد جاء عالم أو فيلسوف من الخارج إلى المحيط الذي نشأ فيه الرسول لما بقي التأثر بهما مجهولاً، فكان على الأقل مذكورًا في تاريخه.
That: If an incident were to occur among them, he would not be ignorant of its place; and that is His saying: 'Did they not recognize their Messenger?' and His saying: 'Those are from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you.' And he grew up illiterate, and the illiterate does not learn from books nor can he remember from the mouths to the utmost degree of memorization; rather his control is through intelligible spiritual forms by which he rises above illusion, evidence of which is that no transmission of poetry like him is found for fear of error and other things, and therefore their amazement at his memorization of the Quran intensified. And Allah said: 'We will make you recite so you shall not forget' and said: 'Do not move your tongue with it to hasten it.' Therefore it was said to the one described with memorization: 'He is more firmly tied ['aqalan?] than the hearts of men from blessings tied with ropes.' Allah said: 'And you did not recite before it any book.' Also, it is not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech and engaging in its various types. Then it is impossible for someone like him to be prepared for what those known for its practice are incapable of. Its proof is that he was not criticized for anything of that, but rather when it was said to him, he said to them: 'Then bring a surah like it' and they were silent and did not claim that he manifested it in it. And that means that if a scholar or philosopher had come from outside to the environment in which the Messenger grew up, the influence of them would not have remained unknown; at least it would have been mentioned in his history.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) from two angles: his lack of prior training in speech and the absence of any external teacher. Maturidi begins by referencing the Quranic verse 'Did they not recognize their Messenger?' implying his character was well-known. He then notes the Prophet's illiteracy—he did not learn from books nor have extraordinary memory; his preservation of the Quran was by divine means, as indicated by 'We will make you recite so you shall not forget.' The author argues that the Prophet was never known to engage in composing poetry or rhetoric, so he could not have produced the Quran. Then he presents the direct proof: when challenged to produce a surah like it, the Quraysh could not, and they did not even accuse him of fabricating it. Finally, Maturidi adds that any external influence from a foreign scholar would have been recorded in history, but no such influence is known. Thus, the Quran is a divine miracle, not human speech.

Key Terms
أمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet's eloquence was a natural talent he cultivated over time.
Correction: Maturidi argues the opposite: he was known for not engaging in rhetoric, and his ability was miraculous.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to show the Quraysh knew the Prophet's character?
A) The verse 'Did they not recognize their Messenger?'
B) The fact that he was illiterate
C) The praise of his companions
D) His wealth and status

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's well-known character and illiteracy remove any possibility that he authored the Quran; it must be divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quraysh knew the Prophet's character and still rejected him. You know his character through seerah—do you let that knowledge compel you to obey every command of his, or do you pick and choose? What area of your life are you ignoring the Prophet's guidance despite knowing his truthfulness?
?
Allah promised the Prophet 'We will make you recite so you shall not forget.' Do you rely on Allah to preserve your faith and good deeds, or do you trust your own efforts? Where are you currently relying on yourself instead of supplicating for divine help?
?
The Prophet's illiteracy is a divine proof that the Quran is not from him. When you feel doubts about the Quran's origin, does this proof truly settle your heart? If not, what is the real barrier in your heart to accepting this evidence?

The Quran's Inimitability and Absence of External Influence
Maturidi argues the Quran's inimitability and the Prophet's isolation from external teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that the Quran is a miracle because the Prophet could not surpass practiced experts and because no external teacher influenced him.

Core Idea
The silence of the critics proves the Quran is inimitable.

Maturidi now presents two further proofs: first, it is impossible for an untrained person to produce something that experts cannot match; second, if an external scholar had taught the Prophet, it would have been recorded in history. The challenge to produce a surah like it was met with silence, confirming its divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the logical flow: from the claim of impossibility to the challenge and the argument from historical silence.
2
Analyze the impossibility argument
Maturidi says it is impossible for someone untrained (the Prophet) to produce what expert poets cannot match. This is a rational proof.
He uses the term 'ممتنع' (impossible).
3
Examine the challenge and response
The Quran challenges the Arabs to produce a surah like it, and they could not. Moreover, they did not even accuse the Prophet of fabricating it.
This silence is evidence.
4
Consider the argument from history
If an external teacher influenced the Prophet, history would mention it. Since there is no such record, the Quran must be from God.
This closes the door to external influence theories.

Proof from the Prophet's Honesty and Rejection of Worldly Gain
Maturidi cites the Prophet's known honesty and his rejection of worldly temptations as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's known honesty over forty years and his rejection of worldly offers serve as proofs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's impeccable character confirms his divine mission.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents two interrelated arguments for the truth of the Prophet's message. First, the verse 'Say: If Allah had willed...' reminds the Quraysh that Muhammad lived among them for forty years before revelation, and they never experienced him lying. Second, despite being offered wealth and leadership to abandon his mission, he refused. This steadfastness, contrary to personal desire, demonstrates that his message is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two Quranic verses cited and the author's commentary on the Prophet's rejection of worldly gain.
Pay attention to the contrast with 'masters of speech' who seek worldly profit.
2
Identify the first proof: the Prophet's known honesty
The verse 'فقد لبثت فيكم عمراً من قبله' points to the Prophet's well-known truthfulness before prophethood. Why would he start lying now? Reflect on how this undermines accusations of falsehood.
The Prophet's impeccable reputation is a rational proof.
3
Understand the second proof: rejection of worldly offers
The passage describes how worldly desires were presented to the Prophet to abandon his religion, but he refused. This shows his sincerity, as he opposed his own natural desires.
Contrast with rhetoricians who seek kings for gain.
4
Reflect on the overall implication
Combining the two proofs, ask yourself: How do the Prophet's past honesty and present steadfastness prove that his message is from God? What does this teach about the character of a true prophet?
This is a key point in establishing prophethood.

قال الله تعالى: ﴿قل لو شاء الله ما تلوته عليكم ولا أدراكم به فقد لبثت فيكم عمراً من قبله أفلا تعقلون﴾. وأيضاً إن الله تعالى أمرهم بتأمل أحواله : هل يجدون ما يعذرهم في ترك الاكتراث إليه، فلم يجدوا؛ قال الله تعالى: ﴿قل إنما أعظكم بواحدة أن تقوموا لله مثنى وفرادى ثم تتفكروا ما بصاحبكم من جنة إن هو إلا نذير لكم بين يدي عذاب شديد﴾ . وأيضا مما دعاهم إلى النظر في أموره أن هل يجدون فيه ما وجدوا في المتسمين بصنعة الكلام من التصدي للملوك لنيل الدنيا ؟ بل عرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليرجع عن دينه مما لديه يعزّ البشر، فلم يجب إلى ذلك، ليُعلم - بالطبيعة المستمرة، على ما فيه مخالفة الهوى وكف النفس عن الملاذ - أنه على ما راضه الله وأكرمه لدار كرامته دون الميل إلى شيء من حطام الدنيا؛ وقال: ﴿قل ما أسألكم عليه من أجر وما أنا من المتكلفين﴾. وأيضاً ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: ﴿قال أو لو جئتكم بأهدى مما وجدتم عليه آباءكم﴾، وقال: ﴿تعالوا إلى كلمة سواء﴾. وأيضا إنه تحداهم بالعجز عما أتى به من القرآن، ليكون حجة له عند امتناعه عن وسع البشر.
Allah said: 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you nor would He have made it known to you; for I have lived among you a lifetime before it. Do you not then reason?' Also, Allah commanded them to reflect on his state: do they find any excuse for themselves in neglecting to heed him? They did not find any. Allah said: 'Say: I only admonish you with one thing: that you stand for Allah in pairs and singly, then reflect - there is no madness in your companion; he is only a warner to you before a severe punishment.' Also, among the things that called them to consider his affairs is: do they find in him what they found in those who are called 'masters of speech' (rhetoricians) in seeking kings for worldly gain? Rather, worldly desires of wealth and leadership were presented to him to abandon his religion, which is rare among humans, but he did not respond to that, so that it is known - by continuous nature, despite opposing desire and restraining the soul from pleasures - that he was as Allah had disciplined and honored him for the abode of His generosity, not inclining to any of the world's worthless things. And he said: 'Say: I ask you not for any reward for it, nor am I of those who pretend.' Also, he challenged them by calling to reflect on religions so that they would know his adherence to the best of what is in intellects, which necessitates choosing the like of it. He said: 'Say: Even if I bring you better than what you found your fathers following?' And he said: 'Come to a common word.' Also, he challenged them with incapability regarding what he brought of the Quran, so that it would be a proof for him when it is beyond human capacity.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage continues the proofs of prophethood with three interconnected arguments. First, Maturidi cites the verse 'Say: If Allah had willed...' to show the Prophet's honesty: he lived among them for forty years before revelation, and they never knew him to lie. Then he references the verse commanding them to reflect on the Prophet's state, finding no madness or falsehood. Second, the author contrasts the Prophet with worldly rhetoricians who seek kings for gain: despite being offered wealth and leadership to abandon his mission, he refused. This sincere endurance, opposing his own desires, proves his mission is from Allah. The verse 'Say: I ask you not for any reward' confirms his disinterest in worldly compensation. Third, Maturidi highlights the Prophet's challenge to reflect on religions and his call to monotheism (the common word). Finally, he reiterates the Quranic challenge: the Quran is beyond human ability, proving its divine origin. Together, these points establish the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Key Terms
لبثت فيكم عمراً
صنعة الكلام
المطامع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's rejection of wealth was merely strategic or could be faked.
Correction: Maturidi argues that his continuous nature and self-control despite opposing desires show it came from divine discipline, not strategy.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to prove that the Prophet was not after worldly gain?
A) The Prophet claimed to be a warner.
B) The Prophet refused offers of wealth and leadership.
C) The Prophet lived among them for forty years.
D) The Prophet challenged them with the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's known honesty and his rejection of worldly temptations together form a strong rational proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet lived among the Quraysh for 40 years without them suspecting him of lying. Reflect: In your own life, is your character consistent with your claims? Do those who know you best see evidence of truthfulness in your daily interactions? What one step can you take this week to align your reputation with your faith?
?
The Prophet rejected wealth and leadership to stay true to his mission. Consider your own attachments: Is there any worldly gain you would not give up for the sake of truth? If you were offered a promotion or relationship that required you to compromise your deen, what would your response be? Are you prepared to say no?
?
The passage says the Prophet's steadfastness shows he was disciplined for God's generosity. Ask yourself: Are your actions driven by craving worldly recognition or by hope for Allah's honor? What evidence do you have in your daily choices that you are not of 'those who pretend' (al-mutakallifin)?

The Quranic Challenge and the Call to Monotheism
Maturidi presents the call to common word and the Quranic challenge as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic challenge to produce a similar scripture and the call to a common word serve as proofs of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability proves it is from Allah.

Imam Maturidi continues his arguments for prophethood by highlighting the Prophet's call to reflect on religions and his challenge with the Quran. The Prophet invited people to a common word of monotheism and challenged them to produce anything like the Quran. Their inability to do so demonstrates that the Quran is beyond human capacity and therefore divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the two elements: the call to reflect and the challenge.
Note the verses 'أو لو جئتكم بأهدى' and 'تعالوا إلى كلمة سواء'.
2
Understand the call to reflection
The passage says the Prophet called them to reflect on religions, showing his adherence to the best of what is in intellects. This invites them to consider that his message aligns with rational truth.
3
Understand the Quranic challenge
The final sentence states that the Prophet challenged them with incapability regarding the Quran. The impossibility of producing something like it serves as a miraculous proof.
This is a classic argument for the Quran's divine origin.
4
Reflect on the combined proof
How do the call to common word and the Quranic challenge together establish the truth of prophethood? Consider that the Quran's inimitability is a direct miracle, while the call to common ground shows the message's universality.

The Prophet's Disinterest in Worldly Gain as Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi presents multiple proofs of prophethood centered on the Prophet's disinterest in worldly gain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's rejection of worldly wealth and his challenges to the Quraysh serve as rational proofs of his prophethood according to Maturidi.

Core Idea
The Prophet's rejection of worldly gain and his challenge to produce like the Qur'an prove his prophethood.

Maturidi, in this passage, offers a cumulative argument for the truthfulness of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). He points to the Prophet's impeccable character, his refusal of material temptations, and his challenge to the Quraysh to produce something similar to the Qur'an. These collectively demonstrate that he is not a pretender but a true messenger of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of Maturidi's argument.
Notice the three distinct proofs: conduct, call to guidance, and Qur'anic challenge.
2
Identify the three proofs
Identify Maturidi's three arguments: (a) the Prophet's rejection of worldly temptations, (b) his call to a common word and better guidance, (c) the challenge to produce the like of the Qur'an.
Each proof builds on the previous one.
3
Reflect on each proof
For each proof, consider why it is compelling. The first shows sincerity, the second shows superiority of message, the third shows divine origin.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Understand how these three proofs together establish that the Prophet is truly sent by God.
This is the overall goal of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدعوا عليه إظهاره فيه . قال الله تعالى: {قل لو شاء الله ما تلوته عليكم}، الآية. وأيضاً إن الله تعالى أمرهم بتأمل أحواله : هل يجدون ما يعذرهم في ترك الاكتراث إليه، فلم يجدوا؛ قال الله تعالى: {قل إنما أعظكم بواحدة}. وأيضا مما دعاهم إلى النظر في أموره أن هل يجدون فيه ما وجدوا في المتسمين بصنعة الكلام من التصدى للملوك لنيل الدنيا ؟ بل عرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليرجع عن دينه مما لديه يَعِزّ البشر، فلم يُجب إلى ذلك، ليُعلم - بالطبيعة المستمرة، على ما فيه مخالفة الهوى وكفّ النفس عن الملاذ - أنه على ما راضه الله وأكرمه لدار كرامته دون الميل إلى شيء من حطام الدنيا؛ وقال: {قل ما أسألكم عليه من أجر وما أنا من المتكلفين} [ص، ٨٦/٣٨]. وأيضاً ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: {قال أو لو جئتكم بأهدى مما وجدتم عليه آباءكم} [الزخرف، ٢٤/٤٣]، الآية . وقال : {تعالوا إلى كلمة سواء}، الآية. وأيضا إنه تحداهم بالعجز عما أتى به من القرآن، ليكون حجة له عند امتناعه عن وسع البشر .
He calls upon them to manifest it in it. Allah the Exalted said: {Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you} – the verse. Also, Allah the Exalted commanded them to contemplate his states: Do they find any excuse for disregarding him? But they did not find any. Allah the Exalted said: {Say: I only admonish you with one thing} – the verse. Also, among the things that called them to look into his affairs is: Do they find in him what they found in those who claim the craft of speech – of seeking after kings for worldly gain? Rather, worldly temptations of wealth and leadership were presented to him to abandon his religion – things that humans cherish – but he did not respond to that, so that it might be known – by his continuous nature, despite opposing desires and restraining the soul from pleasures – that he is upon what Allah has pleased him and honored him for the abode of His honor, without inclination to any of the world's vanities. And he said: {Say: I ask of you no reward for it, nor am I of the pretenders} [Sad 38:86]. Also, he argued with them by calling to consider the religions so that they might know his adherence to the best of what is in intellects, which necessitates choosing the like of it. He said: {Say: Even if I bring you better guidance than what you found your fathers upon} [Zukhraf 43:24] – the verse. And he said: {Come to a common word} – the verse. Also, he challenged them to incapability regarding what he brought of the Qur'an, so that it might be a proof for him when it is beyond human capacity.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood. Maturidi presents several arguments: First, the Prophet's own conduct – he challenges the Quraysh to reflect on his life and see if they can find any worldly motive. Despite being offered wealth and leadership, he refused. This demonstrates his truthfulness, as a liar would have accepted such gains. Maturidi emphasizes that the Prophet's consistent nature, controlling desires and refraining from pleasures, shows he is divinely favored. Second, the Prophet argues that he brings better guidance than ancestral traditions, calling to a common word. Third, he challenges them to produce something like the Qur'an, which is beyond human capacity. Each of these points serves as a proof that the Prophet is truly sent by God.

?

The Qur'an's Superiority Over Poetry and Soothsaying
Maturidi classifies speech and proves Qur'an's inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the classification of speech into poetry and soothsaying to argue for the Qur'an's divine origin.

Core Idea
The Qur'an excels poetry in composition and soothsaying in meaning, proving it is not human speech.

Maturidi begins with a simple observation: elevated speech comes in two distinct types. By showing that the Qur'an surpasses both in their respective strengths, he establishes its uniqueness. This passage lays out that comparison and draws the necessary conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to get the overall argument.
Note that Maturidi uses a classification structure.
2
Identify the two types of craft
Spot the two kinds of elevated speech: poetry (صناعة الشعر) and soothsaying (صناعة الكهانة). Notice Maturidi's description of each.
Poetry is about composition; soothsaying is about meanings.
3
See how the Qur'an surpasses both
Maturidi says the Qur'an excels poetry in composition and soothsaying in meanings. Understand why this leads to the conclusion that it is not human speech.
The word 'musta'liyan' indicates superiority.
4
Reflect on the supporting verses
Review the Quranic verses quoted as evidence. They challenge anyone to produce something like the Qur'an and deny it is poetry.
These verses are part of the challenge (tahaddi) argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع ما وجدت الصناعة التي بها نباهة ورفعة من الكلام نوعان أحدهما صناعة الشعر بالنظم الرائع والتأليف المؤنق . والثاني صناعة الكهانة بإفادة المعاني العربية من تقدم القول على الأشياء الكائنة. ثم وجد القرآن بنظمه مستعليّا على ما جاء به الشعراء، وبمعانيه على ما جاء به الكهنة، فوجب أنه ليس من كلام البشر . وفي مثله احتجاج الله تعالى: {قل لئن اجتمعت الإنس والجن على أن يأتوا بمثل هذا القرآن}، وقوله: {وما هو بقول شاعر}، الآية، وقوله: {أو لم تأتهم بينة}، الآية، وقوله: {كتاب أنزلناه إليك مبارك}. وقوله: {قل فأتوا بكتاب من عند الله}، الآية.
Along with that, I found that the craft which brings distinction and elevation – speech is of two types: one is the craft of poetry with splendid composition and elegant arrangement, and the second is the craft of soothsaying by conveying Arabic meanings from prior statements about future events. Then the Qur'an was found in its composition surpassing what the poets brought, and in its meanings surpassing what the soothsayers brought, so it is necessary that it is not human speech. And similar to this is the argument of Allah Most High: {Say: If all humankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Qur'an}, and His statement: {It is not the speech of a poet}, the verse, and His statement: {Or did not a clear sign come to them}, the verse, and His statement: {A Book We have sent down to you, blessed}, and His statement: {Say: Bring a book from Allah}, the verse.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof. Maturidi identifies two types of elevated speech: poetry, known for its beautiful composition and arrangement, and soothsaying, known for conveying meanings about future events. He then states that the Qur'an excels poetry in its composition and excels soothsaying in its meanings. Therefore, it cannot be human speech. He supports this with Quranic verses that challenge anyone to produce something like the Qur'an, and that deny it is the speech of a poet. This argument is a standard proof of prophethood: the Qur'an's inimitability demonstrates its divine origin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Qur'an is simply excellent poetry or soothsaying.
Correction: Maturidi shows the Qur'an is not merely one of these types but excels both, proving it is categorically different.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the Qur'an's composition prove it is not human speech?
A) Because it is like poetry
B) Because it surpasses both poetry and soothsaying
C) Because it is illogical
D) Because it is like soothsaying

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's excellence in both composition and meaning proves it is not human speech but divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Qur'an proves its divine origin through excellence in both form and content. Have you allowed that proof to settle in your heart, or do you still treat it as just one option among many? What step will you take this week to deepen your conviction in the Qur'an's divine authorship?

Divine Support as Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi presents divine aid to the Prophet as a sign of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the fact of divine support for the Prophet against his opponents as a sign of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Divine aid proves prophethood when all else is dark.

Maturidi presents another powerful argument for the truth of the Prophet's mission: the divine support he received against his opponents. This support was not accidental; it came at a time when guidance was lost and religion had faded. The Prophet was sent to rescue humanity, and Allah did not abandon him. This lesson examines how this support functions as a proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms like 'ta'yid' and 'nusra'.
2
Understand the context of darkness
Maturidi emphasizes that the Prophet was sent during a time of 'obliterated signs of guidance' and 'effaced traces of religion'. Why does this context matter for the proof?
3
Identify the proof structure
The passage states: (1) Allah indicated support that manifests the call and makes the argument successful, (2) He aids the Prophet against opponents, (3) He sent him in a dark time to save people, (4) He did not leave him without support. This sequence shows the proof.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: How does the timing (darkness) and the divine support combine to make a strong sign? How would this convince someone of the Prophet's truthfulness?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوته وبه تفلح حجته بما ينصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى. ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره
Also, what He indicated of the support that manifests his call and makes his argument successful – by which He aids him against those who oppose and contend with him. For Allah the Exalted sent him at a time when the signs of guidance were obliterated and the traces of religion were effaced, to save the servants from perdition. Then when He established him in this noble station and mighty affair, He did not leave him without His support.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is another proof of prophethood. Maturidi points to the divine support and victory granted to the Prophet against his opponents. He emphasizes that Allah sent the Prophet during a time of spiritual darkness when guidance was lost and religious traces were fading. The Prophet was sent to rescue people from destruction. Despite the immense challenge, Allah did not abandon him but provided support, which serves as a sign that the Prophet is truly sent by God.

What does Maturidi mention as another sign of prophethood in this passage?
A) The Prophet's wealth

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face opposition for standing by the truth, do you rely on your own planning or do you truly expect divine support? Think of a specific moment you tried to handle things on your own. What would change if you trusted in Allah's aid like the Prophet did?
?

Prophethood

Divine Support Despite Human Weakness
Maturidi proves prophethood through the Prophet's victory despite total lack of worldly support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the Prophet's lack of worldly power to prove that his success came from divine support.

Core Idea
The Prophet's victory without wealth, clan, or human aid proves divine backing.

Maturidi presents a compelling argument from the Prophet's own circumstances: he was sent in a time of spiritual darkness, without worldly resources, facing intense opposition. Yet he succeeded. This lesson examines how this paradox becomes a proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repeated emphasis on the Prophet's lack of worldly support.
2
Identify the hardships enumerated
List the specific hardships the Prophet faced: sent in an age of spiritual darkness, he had no wealth, no clan (they opposed him), he was expelled.
These are contrasted with the promise of victory.
3
Examine the Qur'anic citations
Find the Qur'anic verses Maturidi cites (e.g., 'We will surely help Our messengers,' 'If you do not help him, Allah has already helped him,' etc.). Understand how they reinforce his argument.
These verses show that divine help is guaranteed regardless of human means.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the overall argument: despite complete lack of human support, the Prophet succeeded. This proves that his strength came from Allah alone, confirming his prophethood.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوته وبه تفلح حجته بما ينصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى. ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره والتمكين له ليقوسى مننه عليه بما أكرمه من المقام بقوله: إنا لننصر رسلنا، الآية، وقوله: كتب الله لأغلبن أنا ورسلى، الآية، وبمثله سبقت كلمته لعباده المرسلين. ثم كان له أيضاً من خصوص حال أن بعث إلى الناس كافة، ووعد له الغلبة والنصر، ليعلم أنه لم يرجع قوته إلى معونة بشرية يتوصل بها طلاب دول الدنيا إلى بغياتهم من إرث ملك في حسبه أو قنية مال ليستمتع بها، بل كان كما قال الله: ووجدك عائلاً فأغنى، الآية؛ ولا عشيرة، بل كانوا أشد الناس عليه وأجهدهم في إطفاء نوره حتى قد أخرجوه من بين أظهرهم طريداً وحيداً؛ ثم مع ذلك لم يدعوا شيئًا مما تشرَه إليه النفس إلا أتوه. فلم يمل إليهم، بل صبر على كل أذى واحتمل كل أمر صعب، فما رضى منهم إلا بالإجابة له في الحق. قال الله تعالى: ولقد جاءكم رسول من أنفسكم، الآية، وقال: وإلا تنصروه فقد نصره الله، الآية، وقال: ويوم حنين إذ أعجبتكم كثرتكم، الآية، وقال: وما أفاء الله له، الآية، وغير ذلك من الآيات والأدلة الصادقة الناطقة أنه بالله قام وبه انتصر.
And also what He indicated of the support (al-taʾyīd) that manifests His call and by which His proof succeeds, with what He helps him against those who oppose and resist him. For Allah Almighty sent him in a time of obliteration of the signs of guidance and erosion of the traces of religion to the servants to rescue them from destruction. Then when He placed him in this noble station and tremendous matter, He did not leave him without His help and empowerment, so that He might complete His favors upon him by what He honored him with of the station, by His saying: 'We will surely help Our messengers,' the verse, and His saying: 'Allah has written: I will surely prevail, I and My messengers,' the verse, and likewise His word preceded for His chosen messengers. Then he also had the particular situation that he was sent to all people, and victory and triumph were promised to him, so that it would be known that his strength did not rely on human assistance through which seekers of worldly states attain their aims of inheriting a kingdom by lineage or acquiring wealth to enjoy. Rather, he was as Allah said: 'And He found you in need and made you self-sufficient,' the verse; and he had no clan, rather they were the most severe of people against him and most striving to extinguish his light until they expelled him from among them, fleeing alone. Then despite that, they did not leave anything that the soul desires except they brought it to him, but he did not incline to them; rather, he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, and he was not satisfied from them except with acceptance of him in truth. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, a messenger has come to you from among yourselves,' the verse, and He said: 'If you do not help him, Allah has already helped him,' the verse, and He said: 'And on the day of Hunayn when your multitude pleased you,' the verse, and He said: 'And what Allah returned to His messenger from them,' the verse, and other such verses and truthful proofs that he stood by Allah and by Him was victorious.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof of prophethood: divine support (taʾyīd) for the Prophet (peace be upon him). Maturidi argues that Allah sent the Prophet in a time of spiritual darkness when guidance and religion were nearly lost, and then gave him a noble mission. Despite the enormity of the task, Allah did not leave him without help and empowerment. Maturidi cites Qur'anic verses promising victory for messengers. He then highlights the particular situation: the Prophet was sent to all people, promised victory, but his strength did not come from human support—he had no wealth or clan. In fact, his own people were the most hostile, expelling him. Despite all temptations, the Prophet did not give in but remained patient and sought only their acceptance of truth. Maturidi concludes by citing several verses showing that Allah's help came despite human weakness, proving the truth of his prophethood.

Key Terms
تأييد
نصر
تمكين
دعوة
حجة
غلبة
عشيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's success was due to human political or military strategy.
Correction: Maturidi emphasizes the Prophet's complete lack of worldly support—no wealth, no clan, and expulsion—showing that his victory was purely by divine help.

Checkpoint
What condition of the Prophet disproves that his victory was due to human power?
A) He was rich and had a large clan.
B) He was poor and had no clan, and was expelled.
C) He had alliances with powerful tribes.
D) He used magic to win.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's victory without any human means is a clear sign that his mission was supported by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face opposition for your faith, do you instinctively rely on your social status, connections, or personal abilities, or do you truly depend on Allah's support as the Prophet did? What are you willing to endure alone for the sake of truth?
?
The Prophet was offered everything the soul desires (wealth, power, acceptance), yet he refused. What worldly temptation are you most attached to that might be hindering your full submission to Allah?
?
Consider a time when you felt utterly alone and powerless. Did you recognize that as an opportunity for divine support, or did you despair? How can you train yourself to see weakness as a channel for Allah's help?

Prophethood Proved by Fulfilled Prophecies
Maturidi presents the argument from fulfilled prophecy and distinguishes it from soothsaying and magic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fulfillment of prophecies about the unseen serves as a rational proof for prophethood and how it differs from soothsaying and magic.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies distinguish true prophets from liars.

Maturidi presents a key argument: prophethood is authenticated by the fulfillment of predictions about the unseen, which no human can know. He contrasts this with soothsaying and magic, which rely on deception and delusion. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall argument before analysis.
2
Identify the argument from fulfillment
Notice that Maturidi starts with the statement that fulfillment of promises regarding the unseen is a proof.
3
Examine the Quranic distinction
The passage quotes Quran 26:221-223 to show that soothsayers receive from devils, while prophets receive from pure angels.
4
Reflect on prophetic consistency
Consider the claim that prophetic actions remain constant truth over time, unlike soothsaying and magic which are based on lies and illusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً مما حاجهم به ما ظهر من إنجاز الموعود في كل ما نطق به مما هو علم الغيب الذي لا يعلمه إلا الله. ومن رام التوصل إليه ببعض الحيل الإنسانية يضل حق ما جاء به في باطله وصدقه في كذبه، ويحصل أمره على تمويه ومخادعة. قال الله تعالى: ﴿هل أنبئكم على من تنزل الشياطين﴾ الآية، فأخبر أن الكهنة يلقون ذلك من إفك الشياطين مما يختطفون، فيحملون على اللمعة من لمع الحق أكاذيب القول وأباطيل الدعوى. والأصل أن الكهانة محمول أكثرها على الكذب والمخادعة، والسحر على الشبه والتخييل. وما اختار الأنبياء يأخذونها على ألسن الملائكة البررة مما لا يوجد فيها غير الصدق والحق، على التجربة والامتحان. وفعلهم حق ثابت على مر الأيام والزمان، ولما أن كان كذلك. ثم وجد كتاب الله ناطقا بإظهار دينه على كل الأديان، مع ما أخبر من الحوادث والأكوان مثل قوله: وهو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى الآية، وقوله: يريدون أن يطفؤوا نور الله بأفواههم الآية، وقوله: أم يقولون نحن جميع منتصر الآية، وقوله: إنا كفيناك المستهزئين، وقوله: قاتلوهم يعذبهم الله بأيديكم الآية، وقوله: أو لم يروا أنا نأتي الأرض ننقصها من أطرافها الآية، وقوله: ولا يزال الذين كفروا تصيبهم الآية، وقوله: وإذ يعدكم الله، وقوله: ولقد صدقكم الله وعده؛ وما جاء من التخصيص في أقوام أنهم لا يؤمنون وأنهم أصحاب الجحيم، ثم ماتوا على الكفر، وغير ذلك مما في كل من الأنباء الغائبة الذي عند التدبر فيها يعلم أنه بالله علمها لتكون آيات له. فمن تأمل ما عددنا من أحوال النبي عليه السلام علم أنه قد انتظمت عنده جميع وجوه البراهين العقلية الدالة على نبوته، وصلى الله على خير البرية.
And also from what he argued against them is what appeared of the fulfillment of the promise in everything he spoke of which is knowledge of the unseen that none knows except Allah. And whoever seeks to attain it by some human tricks goes astray from the truth of what he brought into his falsehood and his truthfulness into his lie, and his affair ends in camouflage and deception. Allah the Exalted said: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?' the verse, and He informed that the soothsayers receive that from the falsehood of the devils from what they snatch, so they combine the flash of truth with lies of speech and false claims. And the origin is that soothsaying is mostly based on lying and deception, and magic on ambiguity and imagination. And what the prophets chose they receive from the tongues of pure angels, in which there is nothing but truth and honesty, by experience and trial. And their action is a constant truth over the passage of days and time. And when that was so, then the Book of Allah was found speaking to manifest His religion over all religions, along with what He informed of events and existences, like His saying: 'It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance' the verse, and His saying: 'They want to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths' the verse, and His saying: 'Or do they say we are a victorious multitude' the verse, and His saying: 'Indeed, We have sufficed you the mockers', and His saying: 'Fight them; Allah will punish them by your hands' the verse, and His saying: 'Do they not see that We come to the land reducing it from its borders' the verse, and His saying: 'And those who disbelieve will not cease to be struck' the verse, and His saying: 'And when Allah promised you one of the two parties', and His saying: 'And Allah had certainly fulfilled His promise to you'; and what came of specification regarding peoples that they would not believe and that they are companions of Hellfire, then they died upon disbelief, and other than that from every one of the unseen tidings which, upon reflection in them, it is known that Allah taught them to be signs for him. So whoever ponders what we have enumerated of the conditions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, knows that all aspects of rational proofs indicating his prophethood have been gathered for him. And may Allah bless the best of creation.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for prophethood by focusing on fulfilled prophecies of unseen matters, distinguishing prophecy from soothsaying and magic. The author begins by stating that the fulfillment of promises (إنجاز الموعود) regarding knowledge of the unseen, which only Allah knows, is a proof. Anyone who tries to imitate this through human tricks ends up in falsehood and deception. Then he quotes the Quranic verse (Surah Ash-Shu'ara, 26:221-223) to show that soothsayers receive from devils, mixing a flash of truth with many lies. Soothsaying (الكهانة) is mostly based on lying and deception, while magic (السحر) is based on delusion and imagination. In contrast, prophets receive revelation from pure angels, which contains only truth and honesty, and this is verified by experience and trial over time. Then the author points to the Quran, which speaks of manifesting the religion over all religions, and lists several Quranic verses that mention events that actually occurred according to divine promise, such as the victory of the religion, the defeat of enemies, and specific judgments about disbelievers dying in unbelief. These are all unseen tidings (أنباء غائبة) that when reflected upon, show they are from Allah and serve as signs. The author concludes that whoever reflects on these conditions of the Prophet realizes that all rational proofs of prophethood are gathered in him.

Key Terms
إنجاز الموعود
علم الغيب
الكهانة
السحر
الملائكة البررة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the origin of soothsaying?
A) Truth from angels
B) Deception from devils
C) Human intelligence
D) Divine revelation

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is proven by the fulfillment of prophecies, which is consistent truth, unlike soothsaying and magic, which are based on lies and deception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever sought knowledge of the unseen through a fortune-teller, astrology, or any other prohibited means? This passage warns that such sources are based on deception. Will you repent and turn solely to the revelation of Allah, which is constant truth?
?
The Prophet’s actions are described as 'constant truth over the passage of days and time.' Does your adherence to his teachings show the same consistency? Identify one area of your life where you compromise the truth of Islam, and commit to correcting it today.
?
The soothsayer mixes a flash of truth with lies. Are there any 'flashes of truth' you have accepted from false sources that have led you away from the straight path? Resolve to abandon them and renew your trust in the Qur'an and Sunnah as your only guide.

Quranic Evidence of Fulfilled Prophecies
Maturidi enumerates Quranic verses containing fulfilled prophecies as evidence for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple Quranic verses serve as examples of fulfilled prophecies that confirm the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Quran itself contains predictions that came true, proving prophethood.

Maturidi continues his argument by presenting Quranic verses that predicted events that later occurred exactly as stated. These unseen tidings (أنباء غائبة) serve as rational proofs for prophethood. This lesson examines those verses and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to see the list of verses Maturidi cites.
2
Identify the predictions
For each verse mentioned, note what was predicted (e.g., victory, punishment, death in disbelief).
3
Understand the rational proof
Reflect on how the fulfillment of these specific predictions, especially about individuals, demonstrates divine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If the Quran's fulfilled prophecies prove that the Prophet spoke from Allah, what is preventing you from fully trusting his message in every aspect of your life—including commands and prohibitions you find difficult?
?
Reflect on one specific prophecy from this lesson (e.g., the preservation of the faith). How does its literal fulfillment confront any doubts you have about the truth of Islam? What change in your daily actions does that certainty demand?
?
The Quran predicts that some people would die in disbelief. Have you considered that you could be among them if you neglect the signs? What concrete step will you take today to ensure you are not among those whom the prophecies condemn?
